<a href="/wiki/.eu" title=".eu">.eu</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[f]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="line-height:11pt"><b>Website</b><br/><span class="url"><a class="external text" href="http://europa.eu" rel="nofollow">europa<wbr/>.eu</a></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>European Union</b> (<b>EU</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Political_union" title="Political union">political</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_union" title="Economic union">economic union</a> of <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">28 member states</a> that are located primarily in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[13]</a></sup> It has an area of  4,475,757 km<sup>2</sup> (1,728,099 sq mi) and an estimated population of over 510 million. The EU has developed <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">an internal single market</a> through a standardised <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">system of laws</a> that apply in all member states in those matters (only) where members have agreed to act as one. EU policies aim to ensure the <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">free movement of people, goods, services and capital</a> within the internal market,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Internal_Market_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Internal_Market-20">[14]</a></sup> enact legislation in justice and home affairs and maintain common policies on trade,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">agriculture</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Common_Fisheries_Policy" title="Common Fisheries Policy">fisheries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regional_policy_of_the_European_Union" title="Regional policy of the European Union">regional development</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[17]</a></sup> For travel within the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Passport_control" title="Passport control">passport controls</a> have been abolished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Internal_borders_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Internal_borders-24">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">A monetary union</a> was established in 1999 and came into full force in 2002 and is composed of <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">19 EU member states</a> which use the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro currency</a>.
</p><p>The EU and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_citizenship" title="European citizenship">European citizenship</a> were established when the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> came into force in 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115-25">[19]</a></sup> The EU traces its origins to the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a> (ECSC) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC), established, respectively, by the 1951 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1951)" title="Treaty of Paris (1951)">Treaty of Paris</a> and 1957 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty of Rome</a>. The original members of what came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a> were the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">Inner Six</a>: Belgium, France, Italy, Luxembourg, the Netherlands, and <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>. The Communities and its successors have grown in size by <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">the accession of new member states</a> and in power by the addition of policy areas to its remit. The latest major amendment to the constitutional basis of the EU, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a>, came into force in 2009. While no member state has <a href="/wiki/Withdrawal_from_the_European_Union" title="Withdrawal from the European Union">left the EU</a> or its antecedent organisations, the United Kingdom <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_invocation_of_Article_50_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union" title="United Kingdom invocation of Article 50 of the Treaty on European Union">signified an intention to leave</a> after a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">membership referendum</a> in June 2016 and is <a href="/wiki/Brexit_negotiations" title="Brexit negotiations">negotiating its withdrawal</a>.
</p><p>Covering 7.3% of the world population,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[20]</a></sup> the EU in 2017 generated a nominal <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) of 19.670 trillion US dollars, constituting approximately 24.6% of global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" title="Nominal GDP">nominal GDP</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[21]</a></sup> and 16.5% when measured in terms of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[22]</a></sup> Additionally, all 28 EU countries have a very high <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Program" title="United Nations Development Program">United Nations Development Programme</a>. In 2012, the EU was awarded the <a href="/wiki/2012_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2012 Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[23]</a></sup> Through the <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a>, the EU has developed a role in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_European_Union" title="Foreign relations of the European Union">external relations</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_European_Union" title="Military of the European Union">defence</a>. The union maintains permanent <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_the_European_Union" title="List of diplomatic missions of the European Union">diplomatic missions</a> throughout the world and <a href="/wiki/European_Union_and_the_United_Nations" title="European Union and the United Nations">represents itself</a> at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_and_the_G7" title="European Union and the G7">G7</a> and the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a>. Because of its global influence, the European Union has been described as an <a href="/wiki/European_Union_as_an_emerging_superpower" title="European Union as an emerging superpower">emerging superpower</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_European_Superpower_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_European_Superpower-30">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="toclimit-3"><div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Union" title="History of the European Union">History of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Europe" title="History of Europe">History of Europe</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ideas_of_European_unity_before_1945" title="Ideas of European unity before 1945">Ideas of European unity before 1945</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IE_expansion.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="275" data-file-width="450" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/IE_expansion.png/220px-IE_expansion.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/IE_expansion.png/330px-IE_expansion.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/IE_expansion.png/440px-IE_expansion.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IE_expansion.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scheme of Indo-European migrations from c. 4000 to 1000 BCE according to the <a href="/wiki/Kurgan_hypothesis" title="Kurgan hypothesis">Kurgan hypothesis</a> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid Magenta; background-color:Magenta; color:black; font-size:60%; text-align:center;"> </span> The assumed <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_Urheimat_hypotheses" title="Proto-Indo-European Urheimat hypotheses">Urheimat</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Samara_culture" title="Samara culture">Samara culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sredny_Stog_culture" title="Sredny Stog culture">Sredny Stog culture</a>) and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Yamna_culture" title="Yamna culture">Yamna culture</a>.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid Red; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:60%; text-align:center;"> </span> Area possibly settled up to c. 2500 BCE.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid Coral; background-color:Coral; color:black; font-size:60%; text-align:center;"> </span> Area settled up to 1000 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeckwith200930_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeckwith200930-31">[25]</a></sup> </div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1540" data-file-width="2534" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/220px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/330px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/440px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Roman Empire in AD 117, at its greatest extent (with its <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassals</a> in pink).</div></div></div>
<p>During the centuries following the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">fall of Rome</a> in 476, several European States viewed themselves as <i><a href="/wiki/Translatio_imperii" title="Translatio imperii">translatio imperii</a></i> of the defunct <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_Empire" title="Frankish Empire">Frankish Empire</a> (481–843) and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> (962–1806) were attempts to resurrect <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Rome in the West</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[g]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Russian Tsardom</a>, and ultimately the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Empire</a> (1547–1917), declared Moscow to be <a href="/wiki/Third_Rome" title="Third Rome">Third Rome</a> and inheritor of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Eastern tradition</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">fall of Constantinople</a> in 1453.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[27]</a></sup> The gap between <a href="/wiki/Greek_East_and_Latin_West" title="Greek East and Latin West">Greek East and Latin West</a> had already been widened by the political scission of the Roman Empire in the 4th century and the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">Great Schism of 1054</a>; and would be eventually widened again by the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> (1945–91).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europe_814.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="919" data-file-width="1399" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Europe_814.svg/220px-Europe_814.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Europe_814.svg/330px-Europe_814.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Europe_814.svg/440px-Europe_814.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europe_814.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a></div></div></div>
<p>Medieval <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[30]</a></sup> and the political power of the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Papacy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[32]</a></sup> are also often cited as conducive to European integration and unity.
</p><p>
Pan-European political thought truly emerged during the 19th century, inspired by the liberal ideas of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolutions</a> after the demise of <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">Napoléon's Empire</a> (1804–15). In the decades following the outcomes of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>, ideals of European unity flourished across the continent, especially in the writings of <a href="/wiki/Wojciech_Jastrz%C4%99bowski" title="Wojciech Jastrzębowski">Wojciech Jastrzębowski</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Mazzini" title="Giuseppe Mazzini">Giuseppe Mazzini</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[34]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Theodore_de_Korwin_Szymanowski" title="Theodore de Korwin Szymanowski">Theodore de Korwin Szymanowski</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[35]</a></sup> The term <i><a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Europe" title="United States of Europe">United States of Europe</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">États-Unis d'Europe</i>) was used at that time by <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugo" title="Victor Hugo">Victor Hugo</a> during a speech at the <a href="/wiki/International_Peace_Congress" title="International Peace Congress">International Peace Congress</a> held in Paris in 1849:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[36]</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europe_1871_map_en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1503" data-file-width="2284" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Europe_1871_map_en.png/220px-Europe_1871_map_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Europe_1871_map_en.png/330px-Europe_1871_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Europe_1871_map_en.png/440px-Europe_1871_map_en.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europe_1871_map_en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Europe in 1871, shaped by vast political units</div></div></div><blockquote><p>A day will come when all nations on our continent will form a European brotherhood ... A day will come when we shall see ... the United States of America and the United States of Europe face to face, reaching out for each other across the seas.</p></blockquote><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a>, the consciousness that national markets in Europe were interdependent though confrontational, along with the observation of a larger and growing US market on the other side of the ocean, nourished the urge for the economic integration of the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[37]</a></sup> In 1920, advocating the creation of a <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European economic union</a>, British economist <a href="/wiki/John_Maynard_Keynes" title="John Maynard Keynes">John Maynard Keynes</a> wrote that "a Free Trade Union should be established ... to impose no protectionist tariffs whatever against the produce of other members of the Union."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[38]</a></sup> During the same decade, <a href="/wiki/Richard_von_Coudenhove-Kalergi" title="Richard von Coudenhove-Kalergi">Richard von Coudenhove-Kalergi</a>, one of the first to imagine of a modern political union of Europe, founded the <a href="/wiki/Paneuropean_Union" title="Paneuropean Union">Pan-Europa Movement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[39]</a></sup> His ideas influenced his contemporaries, among which then <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_France" title="Prime Minister of France">Prime Minister of France</a> <a href="/wiki/Aristide_Briand" title="Aristide Briand">Aristide Briand</a>. In 1929, the latter gave a speech in favour of a European Union before the assembly of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>, precursor of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[40]</a></sup> In a <a class="external text" href="http://www.ibiblio.org/pha/policy/1943/1943-03-21a.html" rel="nofollow">radio address</a> in March 1943, with war still raging, Britain's leader Sir <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> <a class="external text" href="https://winstonchurchill.org/resources/speeches/1941-1945-war-leader/national-address/" rel="nofollow">spoke</a> warmly of "restoring the true greatness of Europe" once victory had been achieved, and mused on the post-war creation of a "Council of Europe" which would bring the European nations together to build peace.
</p><h3><span id="Preliminary_.281945.E2.80.9357.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Preliminary_(1945–57)">Preliminary (1945–57)</span></h3>

<div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schuman_Declaration.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Robert_Schuman" title="Robert Schuman">Robert Schuman</a> <a href="/wiki/Schuman_Declaration" title="Schuman Declaration">proposing</a> the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">Coal and Steel Community</a> on <a href="/wiki/Europe_Day" title="Europe Day">9 May</a> 1950</div></div></div>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a> was seen as an antidote to the extreme nationalism which had devastated the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[41]</a></sup> In a speech delivered on 19 September 1946 at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Z%C3%BCrich" title="University of Zürich">University of Zürich</a>, Switzerland, <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> went further and advocated the emergence of a <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Europe" title="United States of Europe">United States of Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[42]</a></sup> The 1948 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hague_Congress_(1948)" title="Hague Congress (1948)">Hague Congress</a> was a pivotal moment in European federal history, as it led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/European_Movement_International" title="European Movement International">European Movement International</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Europe" title="College of Europe">College of Europe</a>, where Europe's future leaders would live and study together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p>It also led directly to the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> in 1949, the first great effort to bring the nations of Europe together, initially ten of them. However, the Council focused primarily on values - human rights and democracy - rather than on economic or trade issues, and was always envisaged as a forum where sovereign governments could choose to work together, with no supra-national authority. It raised great hopes of further European integration, and there were fevered debates in the two years that followed as to how this could be achieved.
</p><p>But in 1952, disappointed at what they saw as the lack of progress within the Council of Europe, six nations decided to go further and created the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>, which was declared to be "a first step in the federation of Europe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[44]</a></sup> Visionary men such as <a href="/wiki/Alcide_De_Gasperi" title="Alcide De Gasperi">Alcide De Gasperi</a> from Italy, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Monnet" title="Jean Monnet">Jean Monnet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schuman" title="Robert Schuman">Robert Schuman</a> from France, and <a href="/wiki/Paul-Henri_Spaak" title="Paul-Henri Spaak">Paul-Henri Spaak</a> from Belgium understood that coal and steel were the two industries essential for waging war, and that by tying their national industries together, future war between their nations was made impossible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_45-59_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_45-59-52">[45]</a></sup> These men and others are officially credited as the <a href="/wiki/Founding_fathers_of_the_European_Union" title="Founding fathers of the European Union">founding fathers of the European Union</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Treaty_of_Rome_.281957.E2.80.9392.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Treaty_of_Rome_(1957–92)">Treaty of Rome (1957–92)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="680" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/280px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/420px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/560px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The continental territories of the member states of the European Union (European Communities pre-1993), coloured in order of accession</div></div></div>
<p>In 1957, Belgium, France, Italy, Luxembourg, the Netherlands, and West Germany signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty of Rome</a>, which created the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC) and established a <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">customs union</a>. They also signed another pact creating the <a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community">European Atomic Energy Community</a> (Euratom) for co-operation in developing <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear energy</a>. Both treaties came into force in 1958.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_45-59_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_45-59-52">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>The EEC and Euratom were created separately from the ECSC, although they shared the same courts and the Common Assembly.  The EEC was headed by <a href="/wiki/Walter_Hallstein" title="Walter Hallstein">Walter Hallstein</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hallstein_Commission" title="Hallstein Commission">Hallstein Commission</a>) and Euratom was headed by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armand" title="Louis Armand">Louis Armand</a> (<a href="/wiki/Armand_Commission" title="Armand Commission">Armand Commission</a>) and then <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Hirsch" title="Étienne Hirsch">Étienne Hirsch</a>. Euratom was to integrate sectors in nuclear energy while the EEC would develop a customs union among members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 1960s, tensions began to show, with France seeking to limit supranational power. Nevertheless, in 1965 an agreement was reached and on 1 July 1967 the <a href="/wiki/Merger_Treaty" title="Merger Treaty">Merger Treaty</a> created a single set of institutions for the three communities, which were collectively referred to as the <i><a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENA_Merge_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_Merge-55">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jean_Rey_(politician)" title="Jean Rey (politician)">Jean Rey</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">presided over</a> the first merged Commission (<a href="/wiki/Rey_Commission" title="Rey Commission">Rey Commission</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="498" data-file-width="661" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg/220px-West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg/330px-West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg/440px-West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 1989, the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> fell, enabling the union to <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">expand</a> further (<a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> pictured)</div></div></div>
<p>In 1973, the Communities were enlarged to include <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, which later <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_European_Communities_membership_referendum,_1982" title="Greenlandic European Communities membership referendum, 1982">left the Communities</a> in 1985, following a dispute over fishing rights), <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_the_United_Kingdom_to_the_European_Communities" title="Accession of the United Kingdom to the European Communities">United Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENA_First_enlargement_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_First_enlargement-58">[51]</a></sup> Norway had negotiated to join at the same time, but Norwegian voters rejected membership in a <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_European_Communities_membership_referendum,_1972" title="Norwegian European Communities membership referendum, 1972">referendum</a>. In 1979, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1979" title="European Parliament election, 1979">first direct elections</a> to the European Parliament were held.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENA_New_Parliament_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_New_Parliament-59">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> joined in 1981, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> following in 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENA_Enlargement_negotiations_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_Enlargement_negotiations-60">[53]</a></sup> In 1985, the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> paved the way for the creation of open borders without passport controls between most member states and some non-member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[54]</a></sup> In 1986, the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">European flag</a> began to be used by the EEC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[55]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Act" title="Single European Act">Single European Act</a> was signed.
</p><p>In 1990, after <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">the fall of the Eastern Bloc</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> became part of the Communities as part of a <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">reunified Germany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_80-89_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_80-89-63">[56]</a></sup> A close fiscal integration with the introduction of the euro was not matched by institutional oversight making things more troubling. Attempts to solve the problems and to make the EU more efficient and coherent had limited success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[57]</a></sup> With further enlargement planned to include the former <a href="/wiki/Communist_state" title="Communist state">communist states</a> of Central and Eastern Europe, as well as <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a> for candidate members to join the EU were agreed upon in June 1993. The expansion of the EU introduced a new level of complexity and discord.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Maastricht_Treaty_.281992.E2.80.932007.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Maastricht_Treaty_(1992–2007)">Maastricht Treaty (1992–2007)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Euro_banknotes_2002.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="587" data-file-width="800" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Euro_banknotes_2002.png/220px-Euro_banknotes_2002.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Euro_banknotes_2002.png/330px-Euro_banknotes_2002.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Euro_banknotes_2002.png/440px-Euro_banknotes_2002.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Euro_banknotes_2002.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> was introduced in 2002, replacing 12 national currencies. Seven countries have since joined.</div></div></div>
<p>The European Union was formally established when the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>—whose main architects were <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Kohl" title="Helmut Kohl">Helmut Kohl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mitterrand" title="François Mitterrand">François Mitterrand</a>—came into force on 1 November 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115-25">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[58]</a></sup> The treaty also gave the name <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Community" title="European Community">European Community</a> to the EEC, even if it was referred as such before the treaty. In 1995, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> joined the EU.
</p><p>In 2002, euro banknotes and coins replaced national currencies in 12 of the member states. Since then, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> has increased to encompass 19 countries. The euro currency became the second largest reserve currency in the world. In 2004, the EU saw <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">its biggest enlargement to date</a> when <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> joined the Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_00_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_00-66">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Lisbon_Treaty_.282007.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lisbon_Treaty_(2007–present)">Lisbon Treaty (2007–present)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="310" data-file-width="521" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Lisbon Treaty</a> entered into force in 2009</div></div></div>
<p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> became EU members. The same year, <a href="/wiki/Slovenian_euro_coins" title="Slovenian euro coins">Slovenia</a> adopted the euro,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_00_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_00-66">[59]</a></sup> followed in 2008 by <a href="/wiki/Cypriot_euro_coins" title="Cypriot euro coins">Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maltese_euro_coins" title="Maltese euro coins">Malta</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Slovak_euro_coins" title="Slovak euro coins">Slovakia</a> in 2009, by <a href="/wiki/Estonian_euro_coins" title="Estonian euro coins">Estonia</a> in 2011, by <a href="/wiki/Latvian_euro_coins" title="Latvian euro coins">Latvia</a> in 2014, and by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithuania_euro_coins" title="Lithuania euro coins">Lithuania</a> in 2015.
</p><p>On 1 December 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Lisbon Treaty</a> entered into force and reformed many aspects of the EU. In particular, it changed the legal structure of the European Union, merging the <a href="/wiki/Three_pillars_of_the_European_Union" title="Three pillars of the European Union">EU three pillars</a> system into a single legal entity provisioned with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legal_personality" title="Legal personality">legal personality</a>, created a permanent <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a>, the first of which was <a href="/wiki/Herman_Van_Rompuy" title="Herman Van Rompuy">Herman Van Rompuy</a>, and strengthened the position of the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiris2010448_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiris2010448-67">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Treaty_of_Rome_anniversary_group_photograph_2017-03-25_03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Treaty_of_Rome_anniversary_group_photograph_2017-03-25_03.jpg/220px-Treaty_of_Rome_anniversary_group_photograph_2017-03-25_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Treaty_of_Rome_anniversary_group_photograph_2017-03-25_03.jpg/330px-Treaty_of_Rome_anniversary_group_photograph_2017-03-25_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Treaty_of_Rome_anniversary_group_photograph_2017-03-25_03.jpg/440px-Treaty_of_Rome_anniversary_group_photograph_2017-03-25_03.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Treaty_of_Rome_anniversary_group_photograph_2017-03-25_03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Group photograph of European Union heads of government on occasion of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">60th anniversary of the Treaty of Rome</a> in Rome, Italy</div></div></div>
<p>In 2012, the EU received the <a href="/wiki/2012_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2012 Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> for having "contributed to the advancement of peace and reconciliation, democracy, and human rights in Europe."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[63]</a></sup> In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> became the 28th EU member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>From the beginning of the 2010s, the cohesion of the European Union has been tested by several issues, including <a href="/wiki/European_debt_crisis" title="European debt crisis">a debt crisis in some of the Eurozone countries</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_migrant_crisis" title="European migrant crisis">increasing migration from the Middle East</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">United Kingdom's withdrawal from the EU</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCUKREFRESLT_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCUKREFRESLT-72">[65]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">referendum in the UK on its membership of the European Union</a> was held in 2016, with 51.9% of participants voting to leave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTEUBrexit_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEUBrexit-73">[66]</a></sup> The UK formally notified the European Council of its decision to leave on 29 March 2017 initiating the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Article_50_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union" title="Article 50 of the Treaty on European Union">formal withdrawal procedure</a> for leaving the EU, committing the UK to leave the EU on 29 March 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structural_evolution">Structural evolution</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">Treaties of the European Union</a></div>
<p>The following timeline illustrates the <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">integration</a> that has led to the formation of the present union, in terms of structural development driven by international treaties:
</p>
<table cellpadding="1" cellspacing="0" style="font-size:85%; line-height:1.0em; text-align:center; margin:0" width="100%">

<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7" width="8%">1954<br/>1955<br/><b><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brussels#Modification" title="Treaty of Brussels">Modified<br/> Brussels<br/> Treaty</a></b>

<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7" width="8%">1957<br/>1958<br/><b><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Rome <br/> Treaty</a> &amp;<br/> <small><a href="/wiki/Euratom_Treaty" title="Euratom Treaty">EURATOM</a></small></b>

<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7" width="8%">1965<br/>1967<br/><b><a href="/wiki/Merger_Treaty" title="Merger Treaty">Merger<br/> Treaty</a></b>

<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7" width="8%">1975<br/>1976<br/><b><a href="/wiki/TREVI" title="TREVI">Council<br/> Agreement<br/> on TREVI</a></b>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_European_Union" title="Demographics of the European Union">Demographics of the European Union</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Density_of_Population_in_EU_2014.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="609" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Density_of_Population_in_EU_2014.svg/200px-Density_of_Population_in_EU_2014.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Density_of_Population_in_EU_2014.svg/300px-Density_of_Population_in_EU_2014.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Density_of_Population_in_EU_2014.svg/400px-Density_of_Population_in_EU_2014.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Density_of_Population_in_EU_2014.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>EU population density in 2014</div></div></div>
<p>As of  1 January 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=European_Union&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the population of the European Union was about 510.1 million people (6.9% of the world population).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-population-11">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[68]</a></sup> In 2015, 5.1 million children were born in the EU-28, corresponding to a <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> of 10 per 1,000, which is 8 births below the world average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[69]</a></sup> For comparison, the EU-28 birth rate had stood at 10.6 in 2000, 12.8 in 1985 and 16.3 in 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[70]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a> rate was positive at an estimated 0.23% in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, 47.3 million people who lived in the EU were born outside their resident country. This corresponds to 9.4% of the total EU population. Of these, 31.4 million (6.3%) were born outside the EU and 16.0 million (3.2%) were born in another EU member state. The largest absolute numbers of people born outside the EU were in Germany (6.4 million), France (5.1 million), the United Kingdom (4.7 million), Spain (4.1 million), Italy (3.2 million), and the Netherlands (1.4 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanisation">Urbanisation</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_European_Union_by_population_within_city_limits" title="List of cities in the European Union by population within city limits">List of cities in the European Union by population within city limits</a></div><p>
The EU contains about 40 urban areas with populations of over one million, including the two <a href="/wiki/Megacity" title="Megacity">megacities</a> (cities with a population of over 10 million) of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eurostat_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-eurostat-80">[73]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[74]</a></sup> In addition to large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_agglomeration" title="Urban agglomeration">agglomerations</a>, the EU also includes several densely populated polycentric urbanised regions that have no single core but have emerged from the connection of several cities and now encompass a large <a href="/wiki/Metropolis" title="Metropolis">metropolis</a>. The largest of these polycentric metropolis include Rhine-Ruhr with approximately 11.5 million inhabitants (<a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> et al.), <a href="/wiki/Randstad" title="Randstad">Randstad</a> with approx. 8.2 million (<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utrecht" title="Utrecht">Utrecht</a> et al.), <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Rhine-Main" title="Frankfurt Rhine-Main">Frankfurt Rhine-Main</a> with approx. 5.8 million (<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a> et al.), the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Diamond" title="Flemish Diamond">Flemish Diamond</a> with approx. 5.5 million (<a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a> et al.), <a href="/wiki/Upper_Silesian_metropolitan_area" title="Upper Silesian metropolitan area">Upper Silesia</a> with approx. 5.2 million (<a href="/wiki/Katowice" title="Katowice">Katowice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ostrava" title="Ostrava">Ostrava</a> et al.) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Copenhagen" title="Greater Copenhagen">Greater Copenhagen</a> with approx. 4 million (<a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6" title="Malmö">Malmö</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Urban_zones_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Urban_zones-82">[75]</a></sup></p><div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_European_Union" title="Languages of the European Union">Languages of the European Union</a></div>

<tr class="sortbottom">
<td colspan="3" style="text-align:left;">
<p><small>Survey 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[77]</a></sup><br/>

</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The European Union has 24 official languages: <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">Slovene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>. Important documents, such as legislation, are translated into every official language and the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> provides translation for documents and plenary sessions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_Languages_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Languages-87">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the high number of official idioms, most of the institutions use only a handful of working languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[83]</a></sup> The European Commission conducts its internal business in three <i>procedural languages</i> : English, French, and German. Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">European Court of Justice</a> uses French as the working language,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[85]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> conducts its business primarily in English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>Even though <a href="/wiki/Language_policy" title="Language policy">language policy</a> is the responsibility of member states, EU institutions promote multilingualism among its citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[h]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[88]</a></sup> English is the most widely spoken language in the EU, being understood by 51% of the EU population when counting both native and non-native speakers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eurobarometer_Languages_P4_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eurobarometer_Languages_P4-97">[89]</a></sup> German is the most widely spoken mother tongue (spoken by 16% of the EU population.) More than a half (56%) of EU citizens is able to engage in a conversation in a language other than their mother tongue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eurobarometer_Languages_P3_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eurobarometer_Languages_P3-98">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most official languages of the EU belong to the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">language family</a>, represented by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balto-Slavic" title="Balto-Slavic">Balto-Slavic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[i]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Italic_languages" title="Italic languages">Italic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[j]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_Europe" title="Germanic Europe">Germanic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[k]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_languages" title="Hellenic languages">Hellenic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[l]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[m]</a></sup> branches. Some EU languages however, namely <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a> (all three <a href="/wiki/Uralic_languages" title="Uralic languages">Uralic</a>), <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> (<a href="/wiki/Vasconic_languages" title="Vasconic languages">Vasconic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[n]</a></sup>) and  <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a> (<a href="/wiki/Semitic_languages" title="Semitic languages">Semitic</a>) do not belong to Indo-European languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Many_tongues,_one_family_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Many_tongues,_one_family-105">[91]</a></sup> The three official alphabets of the European Union (<a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greek_alphabet" title="Greek alphabet">modern Greek</a>), all derive from the <a href="/wiki/Archaic_Greek_alphabets" title="Archaic Greek alphabets">Archaic Greek scripts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-6">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[92]</a></sup>
</p><p>Besides the 24 official languages, there are about 150 <a href="/wiki/Regional_language" title="Regional language">regional</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minority_language" title="Minority language">minority languages</a>, spoken by up to 50 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Many_tongues,_one_family_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-Many_tongues,_one_family-105">[91]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> are not recognised official languages of the European Union but have semi-official status: official translations of the treaties are made into them and citizens have the right to correspond with the institutions in these languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[94]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages</a> ratified by most EU states provides general guidelines that states can follow to protect their linguistic heritage. The <a href="/wiki/European_Day_of_Languages" title="European Day of Languages">European Day of Languages</a> is held annually on 26 September and is aimed at encouraging language learning across Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[95]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_European_Union" title="Religion in the European Union">Religion in the European Union</a></div>

<th>Affiliation

<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>
</td>
<td align="right"><b>71.6</b>
</td>
<td align="left"><span style="display:none;">71.6</span><div style="width:143.2px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:darkblue"> </div><b></b>
</td></tr>

<td style="text-indent:15px;">Non-believer/<a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">Agnostic</a>
</td>
<td align="right"><b>13.6</b>
</td>
<td align="left"><span style="display:none;">13.6</span><div style="width:27.2px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:lightgrey"> </div><b></b>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-indent:15px;"><a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">Atheist</a>
</td>
<td align="right"><b>10.4</b>
</td>
<td align="left"><span style="display:none;">10.4</span><div style="width:20.8px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:lightgrey"> </div><b></b>
</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>The EU has no formal connection to any religion. The Article 17 of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Functioning_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union">Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[96]</a></sup> recognises the "status under national law of churches and religious associations" as well as that of "philosophical and non-confessional organisations".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Consolidated_Treaties_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Consolidated_Treaties-111">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>The preamble to the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Treaty on European Union</a> mentions the "cultural, religious and humanist inheritance of Europe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Consolidated_Treaties_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-Consolidated_Treaties-111">[97]</a></sup> Discussion over the draft texts of the European Constitution and later the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> included proposals to mention <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> or <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a>, or both, in the preamble of the text, but the idea faced opposition and was dropped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUO_Merkel_God_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUO_Merkel_God-112">[98]</a></sup>
</p><p>Christians in the European Union are divided among members of Catholicism (both <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Roman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Rite</a>), numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> denominations (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglicans" title="Anglicans">Anglicans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutherans" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformed" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> forming the bulk of this category), and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>. In 2009, the EU had an estimated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Muslim_population" title="List of countries by Muslim population">Muslim population</a> of 13 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgmpPRC_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-mgmpPRC-113">[99]</a></sup> and an estimated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_population" title="Jewish population">Jewish population</a> of over a million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[100]</a></sup> The other world religions of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> are also represented in the EU population.
</p><p>According to new polls about religiosity in the European Union in 2015 by <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the largest religion in the European Union, accounting for 71.6% of the EU population. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholics" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> are the largest <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> group, accounting for 45.3% of the EU population, while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestants</a> make up 11.1%, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a> make up 9.6%, and other Christians make up 5.6%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2015_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-EB2015-7">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a> opinion polls showed in 2005 that 52% of EU citizens believed in a God, 27% in "some sort of spirit or life force", and 18% had no form of belief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Religion_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Religion-115">[101]</a></sup> Many countries have experienced falling church attendance and membership in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About_SecE_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-About_SecE-116">[102]</a></sup> The countries where the fewest people reported a religious belief were Estonia (16%) and the Czech Republic (19%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Religion_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Religion-115">[101]</a></sup> The most religious countries were Malta (95%, predominantly Roman Catholic) as well as Cyprus and Romania (both predominantly Orthodox) each with about 90% of citizens professing a belief in God. Across the EU, belief was higher among women, older people, those with religious upbringing, those who left school at 15 or 16, and those "positioning themselves on the right of the political scale".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Religion_115-2"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Religion-115">[101]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_states">Member states</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">Member state of the European Union</a></div>
<p>Through successive <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">enlargements</a>, the European Union has grown from the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">six founding states</a> (Belgium, France, West Germany, Italy, Luxembourg, and the Netherlands) to the current 28. Countries accede to the union by becoming party to the founding <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaties</a>, thereby subjecting themselves to the privileges and obligations of EU membership. This entails a partial delegation of sovereignty to the institutions in return for representation within those institutions, a practice often referred to as "pooling of sovereignty".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>To become a member, a country must meet the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a>, defined at the 1993 meeting of the European Council in Copenhagen. These require a stable democracy that respects human rights and the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a>; a functioning <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>; and the acceptance of the obligations of membership, including EU law. Evaluation of a country's fulfilment of the criteria is the responsibility of the European Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Accession_Criteria_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Accession_Criteria-119">[105]</a></sup> No member state has yet left the Union, although <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_area" title="Autonomous area">autonomous province</a> of Denmark) withdrew in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[106]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Lisbon Treaty</a> now contains a clause under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Article_50_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union" title="Article 50 of the Treaty on European Union">Article 50</a>, providing for a member to <a href="/wiki/Withdrawal_from_the_European_Union" title="Withdrawal from the European Union">leave the EU</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are six countries that are recognised as <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">candidates for membership</a>: <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Albania_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Albania to the European Union">Albania</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accession_of_Iceland_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Iceland to the European Union">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Macedonia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Macedonia to the European Union">Macedonia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[o]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Montenegro_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Montenegro to the European Union">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Serbia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Serbia to the European Union">Serbia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Turkey_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Turkey to the European Union">Turkey</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Enlargement_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Enlargement-123">[108]</a></sup> though Iceland suspended negotiations in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icelandover_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-icelandover-124">[109]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Bosnia and Herzegovina to the European Union">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Kosovo_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Kosovo to the European Union">Kosovo</a> are officially recognised as potential candidates,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Enlargement_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Enlargement-123">[108]</a></sup> with Bosnia and Herzegovina having submitted a membership application.
</p><p>The four countries forming the <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">European Free Trade Association</a> (EFTA) are not EU members, but have partly committed to the EU's economy and regulations: Iceland, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, which are a part of the <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">single market</a> through the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, which has similar ties through <a href="/wiki/Switzerland%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Switzerland–European Union relations">bilateral treaties</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EEA_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-EEA-125">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CH_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-CH-126">[111]</a></sup> The relationships of the <a href="/wiki/Microstates_and_the_European_Union" title="Microstates and the European Union">European microstates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican</a> include the use of the euro and other areas of co-operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euro_use_world_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-euro_use_world-127">[112]</a></sup> The following 28 <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a> (of which the map only shows territories situated in and around Europe) constitute the European Union:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[113]</a></sup>
</p>
