<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_European_Union" title="Geography of the European Union">Geography of the European Union</a></div>
<p>The EU's member states cover an area of 4,423,147 square kilometres (1,707,787 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Area.and.population.figure_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Area.and.population.figure-130">[q]</a></sup> The EU's highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Mont_Blanc" title="Mont Blanc">Mont Blanc</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Graian_Alps" title="Graian Alps">Graian Alps</a>, 4,810.45 metres (15,782 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[114]</a></sup> The lowest points in the EU are <a href="/wiki/Lammefjorden" title="Lammefjorden">Lammefjorden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zuidplaspolder" title="Zuidplaspolder">Zuidplaspolder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, at 7 m (23 ft) below sea level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[115]</a></sup>
The landscape, climate, and economy of the EU are influenced by its coastline, which is 65,993 kilometres (41,006 mi) long.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 189.33333333333px"><div style="width: 189.33333333333px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 187.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Komos_site_baie_Cr%C3%A8te.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2942" data-file-width="4592" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Komos_site_baie_Cr%C3%A8te.jpg/281px-Komos_site_baie_Cr%C3%A8te.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Komos_site_baie_Cr%C3%A8te.jpg/422px-Komos_site_baie_Cr%C3%A8te.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Komos_site_baie_Cr%C3%A8te.jpg/562px-Komos_site_baie_Cr%C3%A8te.jpg 2x" width="188"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The EU's 65,993 km (41,006 mi) coastline dominates the climate. Greece has the longest coastline in the EU (the ancient harbour of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pha%C3%AFstos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Phaïstos (page does not exist)">Phaïstos</a>, Greece).
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162.66666666667px"><div style="width: 162.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 160.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG/241px-Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG/361px-Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG/481px-Mont-Blanc_and_Lake_of_Passy.JPG 2x" width="161"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Mont_Blanc" title="Mont Blanc">Mont Blanc</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> is the highest peak in the EU
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 176.66666666667px"><div style="width: 176.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 174.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parliament_Budapest_Hungary.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1163" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Parliament_Budapest_Hungary.jpg/262px-Parliament_Budapest_Hungary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Parliament_Budapest_Hungary.jpg/393px-Parliament_Budapest_Hungary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Parliament_Budapest_Hungary.jpg/524px-Parliament_Budapest_Hungary.jpg 2x" width="175"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> (pictured in Budapest), is the longest river in the European Union
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 184px"><div style="width: 184px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 182px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hindens_rev_-_KMB_-_16001000011556.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="506" data-file-width="768" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Hindens_rev_-_KMB_-_16001000011556.jpg/273px-Hindens_rev_-_KMB_-_16001000011556.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Hindens_rev_-_KMB_-_16001000011556.jpg/410px-Hindens_rev_-_KMB_-_16001000011556.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Hindens_rev_-_KMB_-_16001000011556.jpg/547px-Hindens_rev_-_KMB_-_16001000011556.jpg 2x" width="182"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4nern" title="Vänern">Vänern</a> in Sweden, the largest lake in the European Union and the third-largest lake entirely in Europe
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<p>Including the overseas territories of France which are located outside the continent of Europe, but which are members of the union, the EU experiences most <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">types of climate</a> from <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">Arctic</a> (North-East Europe) to tropical (<a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>), rendering meteorological averages for the EU as a whole meaningless. The majority of the population lives in areas with a temperate <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime climate</a> (North-Western Europe and Central Europe), a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (Southern Europe), or a warm summer continental or <a href="/wiki/Hemiboreal" title="Hemiboreal">hemiboreal</a> climate (Northern <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and Central Europe).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Humid_Continental_climate_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Humid_Continental_climate-133">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>The EU's population is highly urbanised, with some 75% of inhabitants living in <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a> as of 2006. Cities are largely spread out across the EU, although with a <a href="/wiki/Blue_Banana" title="Blue Banana">large grouping</a> in and around the <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Politics of the European Union">Politics of the European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">Institutions of the European Union</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_European_Union" title="Legislature of the European Union">Legislature of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="1052" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg/400px-Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg/600px-Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg/800px-Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Organigram of the political system with the seven institutions of the Unio in blue, national / intergovernmental elements in orange</div></div></div>
<p>The EU operates through a hybrid system of <a href="/wiki/Supranational_union" title="Supranational union">supranational</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmentalism" title="Intergovernmentalism">intergovernmental</a> decision-making,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-135">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-136">[119]</a></sup>and according to the principles of <a href="/wiki/Principle_of_conferral" title="Principle of conferral">conferral</a> (which says that it should act only within the limits of the competences conferred on it by the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaties</a>) and of <a href="/wiki/Subsidiarity#European_Union_law" title="Subsidiarity">subsidiarity</a> (which says that it should act only where an objective cannot be sufficiently achieved by the member states acting alone). <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">Laws made by the EU institutions</a> are passed in a variety of forms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[120]</a></sup> Generally speaking, they can be classified into two groups: those which come into force without the necessity for national implementation measures (regulations) and those which specifically require national implementation measures (directives).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p>The European Union has seven principal decision making bodies, its <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">institutions</a>: the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a>,  the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union" title="Court of Justice of the European Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Auditors" title="European Court of Auditors">European Court of Auditors</a>. Competence in scrutinising and amending legislation is shared between the Council of the European Union and the European Parliament, while executive tasks are performed by the European Commission and in a limited capacity by the European Council (not to be confused with the aforementioned Council of the European Union). The <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary policy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> is determined by the European Central Bank. The interpretation and the application of EU law and the treaties are ensured by the Court of Justice of the European Union. The EU budget is scrutinised by the European Court of Auditors. There are also a number of ancillary bodies which advise the EU or operate in a specific area.
</p>
<ul><li>the <b><a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a></b>, which sets the <i>general political directions</i> and <i>priorities</i> of the Union by gathering together its member states' <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">heads of state</a>/<a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">government</a> (elected chief executives). The conclusions of its summits (held at least quarterly) are adopted by consensus.</li>
<li>the <b><a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a></b>, the "Guardian of the Treaties" consists of an <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">executive cabinet</a> of public officials, led by an <a href="/wiki/Indirect_election" title="Indirect election">indirectly elected</a> President. This <i>College of Commissioners</i> manages and directs the Commission's permanent civil service. It turns the consensus objectives of the European Council into <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">legislative proposals</a>.</li>
<li>the <b><a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a></b> brings together ministers of member states governments' departments. It forms the <i><a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a></i> of the EU's essentially <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral legislature</a> and its approval is required for any proposal to enter into law.</li>
<li>the <b><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a></b> consists of 751 directly elected representatives, forming the EU's <i><a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a></i> of its bicameral legislature. It shares with the Council of the EU equal legislative powers to amend, approve or reject Commission proposals for most areas of EU legislation. Its powers are limited in areas where member states' view sovereignty to be of primary concern (i.e. defence). It elects the Commission's President, must approve the College of Commissioners, and may vote to remove them collectively from office.</li>
<li>the <b><a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union" title="Court of Justice of the European Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</a></b> ensures the uniform application of EU law and resolves disputes between EU institutions and member states, and against EU institutions on behalf of individuals.</li>
<li>the <b><a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a></b> is responsible for monetary stability within member states.</li>
<li>the <b><a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Auditors" title="European Court of Auditors">European Court of Auditors</a></b> investigates the proper management of finances within both the EU entities and EU funding provided to its member states. As well as providing oversight and advice, it can refer unresolved issues to the European Court of Justice to arbitrate on any alleged irregularities.</li></ul>
<p>EU policy is in general promulgated by <a href="/wiki/Directive_(European_Union)" title="Directive (European Union)">EU directives</a>, which are then implemented in the <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">domestic legislation</a> of its <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member states</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Regulation_(European_Union)" title="Regulation (European Union)">EU regulations</a>, which are immediately enforceable in all member states. <a href="/wiki/Lobbying#European_Union" title="Lobbying">Lobbying</a> at EU level by special interest groups is regulated to try to balance the aspirations of private initiatives with public interest decision-making process<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[122]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament">European Parliament</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3389" data-file-width="6000" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/220px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/330px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/440px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Hemicycle" title="Hemicycle">hemicycle</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> in Strasbourg</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> forms the other half of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_European_Union" title="Legislature of the European Union">EU's legislature</a>.
The 751 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Members of the European Parliament</a> (MEPs) are directly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_European_Union" title="Elections in the European Union">elected</a> by <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">EU citizens</a> every five years on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>. Although MEPs are elected on a national basis, they sit according to <a href="/wiki/Political_groups_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Political groups of the European Parliament">political groups</a> rather than their nationality. Each country has a set number of seats and is divided into <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_constituency" title="European Parliament constituency">sub-national constituencies</a> where this does not affect the proportional nature of the voting system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[123]</a></sup>
</p><p>The European Parliament and the Council of the European Union pass legislation jointly in nearly all areas under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ordinary_legislative_procedure" title="Ordinary legislative procedure">ordinary legislative procedure</a>. This also applies to the <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">EU budget</a>. The European Commission is accountable to Parliament, requiring its approval to take office, having to report back to it and subject to motions of censure from it. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="President of the European Parliament">President of the European Parliament</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Tajani" title="Antonio Tajani">Antonio Tajani</a>) carries out the role of speaker in Parliament and represents it externally. The President and <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Vice President of the European Parliament">Vice-Presidents</a> are elected by MEPs every two and a half years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Institutions_Parliament_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Institutions_Parliament-141">[124]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Council">European Council</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1550" data-file-width="1200" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg/170px-Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg/255px-Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg/340px-Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Donald_Tusk_2013-12-19.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Tusk" title="Donald Tusk">Donald Tusk</a></div></div></div>
<p>The European Council gives political direction to the EU. It convenes at least four times a year and comprises the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Donald_Tusk" title="Donald Tusk">Donald Tusk</a>), the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a> and one representative per <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member state</a> (either its <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> or <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>). The <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Federica_Mogherini" title="Federica Mogherini">Federica Mogherini</a>) also takes part in its meetings. It has been described by some as the Union's "supreme political authority".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-How_work_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-How_work-142">[125]</a></sup> It is actively involved in the negotiation of <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaty changes</a> and defines the EU's policy agenda and strategies.
</p><p>The European Council uses its leadership role to sort out disputes between member states and the institutions, and to resolve political crises and disagreements over controversial issues and policies. It acts externally as a "<a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">collective head of state</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Ratification" title="Ratification">ratifies</a> important documents (for example, international agreements and treaties).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tasks for the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a> are ensuring the external representation of the EU,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Council_Press_Release_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-Council_Press_Release-144">[127]</a></sup> driving consensus and resolving divergences among member states, both during meetings of the European Council and over the periods between them.
</p><p>The European Council should not be mistaken for the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, an international organisation independent of the EU based in Strasbourg.
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Council_of_the_European_Union">Council of the European Union</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> (also called the "Council"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[128]</a></sup> and the "Council of Ministers", its former title)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[129]</a></sup> forms one half of the EU's legislature. It consists of a <a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">government minister</a> from each member state and meets in <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union#Configurations" title="Council of the European Union">different compositions depending on the policy area being addressed</a>. Notwithstanding its different configurations, it is considered to be one single body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Institutions_Council_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Institutions_Council-147">[130]</a></sup> In addition to its legislative functions, the Council also exercises <a href="/wiki/Executive_functions" title="Executive functions">executive functions</a> in relations to the <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a>.
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<p>In some policies, there are several member states that ally with strategic partners within the Union. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visegrad_Group" title="Visegrad Group">Visegrad Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Assembly" title="Baltic Assembly">Baltic Assembly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Council" title="Nordic Council">Nordic Council</a> or <a href="/wiki/Craiova_Group" title="Craiova Group">Craiova Group</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Commission">European Commission</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1691" data-file-width="1225" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg/170px-Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg/255px-Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg/340px-Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ioannes_Claudius_Juncker_die_7_Martis_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">Commission President</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> acts as the EU's <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive arm</a> and is responsible for <a href="/wiki/Right_of_initiative_(legislative)" title="Right of initiative (legislative)">initiating legislation</a> and the day-to-day running of the EU. The Commission is also seen as the motor of <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>. It operates as a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet government</a>, with 28 <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner" title="European Commissioner">Commissioners</a> for different areas of policy, one from each member state, though Commissioners are bound to represent the interests of the EU as a whole rather than their home state.
</p><p>One of the 28 is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a>) appointed by the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>. After the President, the most prominent Commissioner is the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy</a>, who is <i>ex-officio</i> a <a href="/wiki/Vice-President_of_the_European_Commission" title="Vice-President of the European Commission">Vice-President of the Commission</a> and is also chosen by the European Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[131]</a></sup> The other 26 Commissioners are subsequently appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> in agreement with the nominated President. The 28 Commissioners as a single body are subject to a vote of approval by the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget">Budget</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">Budget of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">

<p>The 2011 EU budget (€141.9 bn)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[132]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8CE; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Cohesion and competitiveness for growth and employment (45%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C67; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Direct aids and market related expenditures (31%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #4A9; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Rural development (11%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #DC7; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> EU as a global partner (6%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:silver; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Administration (6%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #A49; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Citizenship, freedom, security and justice (1%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p>The EU had an agreed budget of €120.7 billion for the year 2007 and €864.3 billion for the period 2007–2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[133]</a></sup> representing 1.10% and 1.05% of the EU-27's <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">GNI</a> forecast for the respective periods. In 1960, the budget of the then European Economic Community was 0.03% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2010 budget of €141.5 billion, the largest single expenditure item is "<i><a href="/wiki/Structural_Funds_and_Cohesion_Fund" title="Structural Funds and Cohesion Fund">cohesion &amp; competitiveness</a></i>" with around 45% of the total budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-152">[135]</a></sup> Next comes "<i><a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">agriculture</a></i>" with approximately 31% of the total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-152">[135]</a></sup> "<i>Rural development, environment and <a href="/wiki/Common_Fisheries_Policy" title="Common Fisheries Policy">fisheries</a></i>" takes up around 11%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_152-2"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-152">[135]</a></sup> "<i>Administration</i>" accounts for around 6%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_152-3"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-152">[135]</a></sup> The "<i>EU as a global partner</i>" and "<i>citizenship, freedom, security and justice</i>" bring up the rear with approximately 6% and 1% respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_152-4"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-152">[135]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Court_of_Auditors" title="Court of Auditors">Court of Auditors</a> is legally obliged to provide the Parliament and the Council with "a statement of assurance as to the reliability of the accounts and the legality and regularity of the underlying transactions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[136]</a></sup> The Court also gives opinions and proposals on financial legislation and anti-fraud actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Institutions_Auditors_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Institutions_Auditors-154">[137]</a></sup> The Parliament uses this to decide whether to approve the Commission's handling of the budget.
</p><p>The European Court of Auditors has signed off the European Union accounts every year since 2007 and, while making it clear that the European Commission has more work to do, has highlighted that most of the errors take place at national level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Court_of_Auditors_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-European_Court_of_Auditors-155">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Commission_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-European_Commission-156">[139]</a></sup> In their report on 2009 the auditors found that five areas of Union expenditure, <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">agriculture</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Structural_Funds_and_Cohesion_Fund" title="Structural Funds and Cohesion Fund">cohesion fund</a>, were materially affected by error.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[140]</a></sup> The European Commission estimated in 2009 that the financial effect of irregularities was €1,863 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[141]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competences">Competences</span></h3>
<p>EU member states retain all powers not explicitly handed to the European Union. In some areas the EU enjoys exclusive competence. These are areas in which member states have renounced any capacity to enact legislation. In other areas the EU and its member states share the competence to legislate. While both can legislate, member states can only legislate to the extent to which the EU has not. In other policy areas the EU can only co-ordinate, support and supplement member state action but cannot enact legislation with the aim of harmonising national laws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>That a particular policy area falls into a certain category of competence is not necessarily indicative of what <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_European_Union" title="Legislature of the European Union">legislative procedure</a> is used for enacting legislation within that policy area. Different legislative procedures are used within the same category of competence, and even with the same policy area.
</p><p>The distribution of competences in various policy areas between Member States and the Union is divided in the following three categories:
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">European Union law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">Treaties of the European Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_(1674586821).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg/220px-European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg/330px-European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg/440px-European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_(1674586821).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">Court of Justice</a>, seated in Luxembourg</div></div></div>
<p>The EU is based on a series of <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaties</a>. These first established the European Community and the EU, and then made amendments to those founding treaties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[143]</a></sup> These are power-giving treaties which set broad policy goals and establish institutions with the necessary legal powers to implement those goals. These legal powers include the ability to enact legislation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art249_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-art249-161">[r]</a></sup> which can directly affect all member states and their inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Direct_Effect_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Direct_Effect-162">[s]</a></sup> The EU has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legal_personality" title="Legal personality">legal personality</a>, with the right to sign agreements and international treaties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>Under the principle of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supremacy_(European_Union_law)" title="Supremacy (European Union law)">supremacy</a>, national courts are required to enforce the treaties that their member states have ratified, and thus the laws enacted under them, even if doing so requires them to ignore conflicting national law, and (within limits) even constitutional provisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Supremacy_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-Supremacy-164">[t]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Courts_of_Justice">Courts of Justice</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parada_R%C3%B3wno%C5%9Bci_2018_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2359" data-file-width="1769" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Parada_R%C3%B3wno%C5%9Bci_2018_01.jpg/170px-Parada_R%C3%B3wno%C5%9Bci_2018_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Parada_R%C3%B3wno%C5%9Bci_2018_01.jpg/255px-Parada_R%C3%B3wno%C5%9Bci_2018_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Parada_R%C3%B3wno%C5%9Bci_2018_01.jpg/340px-Parada_R%C3%B3wno%C5%9Bci_2018_01.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parada_R%C3%B3wno%C5%9Bci_2018_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Parada_R%C3%B3wno%C5%9Bci" title="Parada Równości">Parada Równości</a>, Warsaw In 2018, the Court of Justice declared same-sex spouses have EU residence rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[145]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial branch</a> of the EU—formally called the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union" title="Court of Justice of the European Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</a>—consists of two courts: the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">Court of Justice</a> and the <a href="/wiki/General_Court_(European_Union)" title="General Court (European Union)">General Court</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[146]</a></sup>
The Court of Justice primarily deals with cases taken by member states, the institutions, and <a href="/wiki/Preliminary_ruling" title="Preliminary ruling">cases referred to it</a> by the courts of member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[147]</a></sup> The General Court mainly deals with cases taken by individuals and companies directly before the EU's courts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[148]</a></sup> and the European Union Civil Service Tribunal adjudicates in disputes between the European Union and <a href="/wiki/European_Civil_Service" title="European Civil Service">its civil service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[149]</a></sup> Decisions from the General Court can be appealed to the Court of Justice but only on a point of law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[150]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fundamental_rights">Fundamental rights</span></h3>
<p>The treaties declare that the EU itself is "founded on the values of respect for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_dignity" title="Human dignity">human dignity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberty" title="Liberty">freedom</a>, democracy, <a href="/wiki/Equality_before_the_law" title="Equality before the law">equality</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a> and respect for human rights, including the rights of persons belonging to <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">minorities</a> ... in a society in which pluralism, non-discrimination, tolerance, justice, solidarity and equality between women and men prevail."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[151]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" title="Lisbon Treaty">Lisbon Treaty</a> gave legal effect to the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union</a>. The charter is a codified catalogue of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fundamental_right" title="Fundamental right">fundamental rights</a> against which the EU's legal acts can be judged. It consolidates many rights which were previously recognised by the Court of Justice and derived from the "constitutional traditions common to the member states."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[152]</a></sup> The Court of Justice has long recognised fundamental rights and has, on occasion, invalidated EU legislation based on its failure to adhere to those fundamental rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-europarl-rights_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-europarl-rights-173">[153]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although signing the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a> (ECHR) is a condition for EU membership,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[u]</a></sup> previously, the EU itself could not accede to the Convention as it is neither a state<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[v]</a></sup> nor had the competence to accede.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[w]</a></sup> The Lisbon Treaty and Protocol 14 to the ECHR have changed this: the former binds the EU to accede to the Convention while the latter formally permits it.
</p><p>Although, the EU is independent from Council of Europe, they share purpose and ideas especially on rule of law, human rights and democracy. Further <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Social_Charter" title="European Social Charter">European Social Charter</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Source_of_law" title="Source of law">source of law</a> of <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights</a> are created by Council of Europe. The EU also promoted human rights issues in the wider world. The EU opposes the death penalty and has proposed its worldwide abolition. Abolition of the death penalty is a condition for EU membership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[154]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acts">Acts</span></h3>
<p>The main legal acts of the EU come in three forms: <a href="/wiki/Regulation_(European_Union)" title="Regulation (European Union)">regulations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Directive_(European_Union)" title="Directive (European Union)">directives</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Decision_(European_Union)" title="Decision (European Union)">decisions</a>. Regulations become law in all member states the moment they come into force, without the requirement for any implementing measures,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[x]</a></sup> and automatically override conflicting domestic provisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art249_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-art249-161">[r]</a></sup> Directives require member states to achieve a certain result while leaving them discretion as to how to achieve the result. The details of how they are to be implemented are left to member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[y]</a></sup> When the time limit for implementing directives passes, they may, under certain conditions, have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_effect" title="Direct effect">direct effect</a> in national law against member states.
</p><p>Decisions offer an alternative to the two above modes of legislation. They are legal acts which only apply to specified individuals, companies or a particular member state. They are most often used in <a href="/wiki/Competition_law" title="Competition law">competition law</a>, or on rulings on State Aid, but are also frequently used for procedural or administrative matters within the institutions. Regulations, directives, and decisions are of equal legal value and apply without any formal hierarchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[155]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Justice_and_home_affairs">Justice and home affairs</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Area_of_freedom,_security_and_justice" title="Area of freedom, security and justice">Area of freedom, security and justice</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frontex_HQ_Warsaw_Spire_office_complex_Warsaw.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4339" data-file-width="3279" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Frontex_HQ_Warsaw_Spire_office_complex_Warsaw.jpg/170px-Frontex_HQ_Warsaw_Spire_office_complex_Warsaw.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Frontex_HQ_Warsaw_Spire_office_complex_Warsaw.jpg/255px-Frontex_HQ_Warsaw_Spire_office_complex_Warsaw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Frontex_HQ_Warsaw_Spire_office_complex_Warsaw.jpg/340px-Frontex_HQ_Warsaw_Spire_office_complex_Warsaw.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frontex_HQ_Warsaw_Spire_office_complex_Warsaw.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seat of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frontex" title="Frontex">Frontex</a> in Warsaw, Poland</div></div></div>
<p>Since the creation of the EU in 1993, it has developed its competencies in the area of justice and home affairs; initially at an intergovernmental level and later by supranationalism. Accordingly, the Union has legislated in areas such as <a href="/wiki/European_Arrest_Warrant" title="European Arrest Warrant">extradition</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[156]</a></sup> family law,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[157]</a></sup> asylum law,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[158]</a></sup> and criminal justice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[159]</a></sup> Prohibitions against sexual and nationality discrimination have a long standing in the treaties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art39/141_Rome_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-art39/141_Rome-185">[z]</a></sup> In more recent years, these have been supplemented by powers to legislate against discrimination based on race, religion, disability, age, and sexual orientation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art2(7)_Amsterdam_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-art2(7)_Amsterdam-186">[aa]</a></sup> By virtue of these powers, the EU has enacted legislation on <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">sexual discrimination</a> in the work-place, <a href="/wiki/Ageism" title="Ageism">age discrimination</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racial discrimination</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[ab]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Union has also established agencies to co-ordinate police, prosecutorial and immigrations controls accross the member states: <a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">Europol</a> for co-operation of police forces,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[160]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eurojust" title="Eurojust">Eurojust</a> for co-operation between prosecutors,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[161]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frontex" title="Frontex">Frontex</a> for co-operation between border control authorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[162]</a></sup> The EU also operates the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Information_System" title="Schengen Information System">Schengen Information System</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Internal_borders_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Internal_borders-24">[18]</a></sup> which provides a common database for police and immigration authorities. This co-operation had to particularly be developed with the advent of open borders through the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> and the associated cross border crime.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_European_Union" title="Foreign relations of the European Union">Foreign relations of the European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_External_Action_Service" title="European External Action Service">European External Action Service</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG/400px-EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG/600px-EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG/800px-EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EU_free_trade_agreements.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>EU Free trade agreements (2017) <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:lightblue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> European Union</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Agreement in force</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:lightgreen; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Pending</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:darkorange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Negotiating</div></div></div></div>
<p>Foreign policy co-operation between member states dates from the establishment of the Community in 1957, when member states negotiated as a bloc in international trade negotiations under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU%27s_common_commercial_policy" title="EU's common commercial policy">EU's common commercial policy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[163]</a></sup> Steps for a more wide-ranging co-ordination in foreign relations began in 1970 with the establishment of <a href="/wiki/European_Political_Cooperation" title="European Political Cooperation">European Political Cooperation</a> which created an informal consultation process between member states with the aim of forming common foreign policies. It was not, however, until 1987 when European Political Cooperation was introduced on a formal basis by the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Act" title="Single European Act">Single European Act</a>. EPC was renamed as the <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a> (CFSP) by the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPC_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPC-192">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p>The aims of the CFSP are to promote both the EU's own interests and those of the <a href="/wiki/International_community" title="International community">international community</a> as a whole, including the furtherance of international co-operation, respect for human rights, democracy, and the rule of law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art11_Union_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-art11_Union-193">[165]</a></sup> The CFSP requires unanimity among the member states on the appropriate policy to follow on any particular issue. The unanimity and difficult issues treated under the CFSP sometimes lead to disagreements, such as those which occurred over the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">war in Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Iraq_statement_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Iraq_statement-194">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>The coordinator and representative of the CFSP within the EU is the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy</a> who speaks on behalf of the EU in foreign policy and defence matters, and has the task of articulating the positions expressed by the member states on these fields of policy into a common alignment. The High Representative heads up the <a href="/wiki/European_External_Action_Service" title="European External Action Service">European External Action Service</a> (EEAS), a unique EU department<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23Oct_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-23Oct-195">[167]</a></sup> that has been officially implemented and operational since 1 December 2010 on the occasion of the first anniversary of the entry into force of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[168]</a></sup> The EEAS will serve as a foreign ministry and <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_corps" title="Diplomatic corps">diplomatic corps</a> for the European Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_EEAS_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_EEAS-197">[169]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">

</p>
