</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<p>Besides the emerging international policy of the European Union, the international influence of the EU is also felt through <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">enlargement</a>. The perceived benefits of becoming a member of the EU act as an incentive for both political and economic reform in states wishing to fulfil the EU's accession criteria, and are considered an important factor contributing to the reform of European formerly Communist countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>762</span></sup> This influence on the internal affairs of other countries is generally referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Soft_power" title="Soft power">soft power</a>", as opposed to military "hard power".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soft_Power_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soft_Power-199">[171]</a></sup>
</p><p>The European Union has concluded <a href="/wiki/European_Union_free_trade_agreements" title="European Union free trade agreements">free trade agreements</a> (FTAs)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[172]</a></sup> and other agreements with a trade component with many countries worldwide and is negotiating with many others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[173]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defence">Defence</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Common_Security_and_Defence_Policy" title="Common Security and Defence Policy">Common Security and Defence Policy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2037" data-file-width="3683" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg/220px-NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg/330px-NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg/440px-NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Out of the 28 EU member states, 22 are also members of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. Another three NATO members are EU applicants—Albania, Montenegro and Turkey.</div></div></div>
<p>The predecessors of the European Union were not devised as a military alliance because <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> was largely seen as appropriate and sufficient for defence purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilkinson2007100_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilkinson2007100-202">[174]</a></sup> 22 EU members are members of NATO<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[175]</a></sup> while the remaining member states follow policies of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutrality_(international_relations)" title="Neutrality (international relations)">neutrality</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[176]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Western_European_Union" title="Western European Union">Western European Union</a>, a military alliance with a mutual defence clause, was disbanded in 2010 as its role had been transferred to the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[177]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute" title="Stockholm International Peace Research Institute">Stockholm International Peace Research Institute</a> (SIPRI), the United Kingdom spent $61 billion on defence in 2014, placing it fifth in the world, while France spent $53 billion, the sixth largest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[178]</a></sup> Together, the UK and France account for approximately 40 per cent of European countries' defence budget and 50 per cent of their military capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[179]</a></sup> Both are officially recognised <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_nuclear_weapons" title="List of states with nuclear weapons">nuclear weapon states</a> holding <a href="/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council">permanent seats</a> on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>.
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a> in 1999, the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> agreed that "the Union must have the capacity for autonomous action, backed by credible military forces, the means to decide to use them, and the readiness to do so, in order to respond to international crises without prejudice to actions by NATO". To that end, a number of efforts were made to increase the EU's military capability, notably the <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Headline_Goal" title="Helsinki Headline Goal">Helsinki Headline Goal</a> process. After much discussion, the most concrete result was the <a href="/wiki/EU_Battlegroup" title="EU Battlegroup">EU Battlegroups</a> initiative, each of which is planned to be able to deploy quickly about 1500 personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Council_Capabilities_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Council_Capabilities-208">[180]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EUFOR" title="EUFOR">EU forces</a> have been deployed on peacekeeping missions from middle and northern Africa to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Balkans" title="Western Balkans">western Balkans</a> and western Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Council_Operations_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Council_Operations-209">[181]</a></sup> EU military operations are supported by a number of bodies, including the <a href="/wiki/European_Defence_Agency" title="European Defence Agency">European Defence Agency</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Satellite_Centre" title="European Union Satellite Centre">European Union Satellite Centre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Military_Staff" title="European Union Military Staff">European Union Military Staff</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Council_Structures_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Council_Structures-210">[182]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frontex" title="Frontex">Frontex</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Agencies_of_the_European_Union" title="Agencies of the European Union">agency of the EU</a> established to manage the cooperation between national <a href="/wiki/Border_guard" title="Border guard">border guards</a> securing its external <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">borders</a>. It aims to detect and stop illegal immigration, <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a> and terrorist infiltration. In 2015 the European Commission presented its proposal for a new European Border and Coast Guard Agency having a stronger role and mandate along with national authorities for border management. In an EU consisting of 28 members, substantial security and defence co-operation is increasingly relying on collaboration among all member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[183]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_aid">Humanitarian aid</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_European_Civil_Protection_and_Humanitarian_Aid_Operations" title="Directorate-General for European Civil Protection and Humanitarian Aid Operations">Directorate-General for European Civil Protection and Humanitarian Aid Operations</a></div>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IAHV,_Jordan_Program_At_Syrian_Refugee_Camp.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/IAHV%2C_Jordan_Program_At_Syrian_Refugee_Camp.jpg/240px-IAHV%2C_Jordan_Program_At_Syrian_Refugee_Camp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/IAHV%2C_Jordan_Program_At_Syrian_Refugee_Camp.jpg/360px-IAHV%2C_Jordan_Program_At_Syrian_Refugee_Camp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/IAHV%2C_Jordan_Program_At_Syrian_Refugee_Camp.jpg/480px-IAHV%2C_Jordan_Program_At_Syrian_Refugee_Camp.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The European Union co-funds <a href="/wiki/Psychosocial" title="Psychosocial">psychosocial</a> support by the IAHV, Jordan at the <a href="/wiki/Zaatari_refugee_camp" title="Zaatari refugee camp">Zaatari refugee camp</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syrian_refugees" title="Syrian refugees">Syrian refugees</a>
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 181.33333333333px"><div style="width: 181.33333333333px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 179.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ECHO_plane.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="535" data-file-width="800" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/ECHO_plane.jpg/269px-ECHO_plane.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/ECHO_plane.jpg/404px-ECHO_plane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/ECHO_plane.jpg/539px-ECHO_plane.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>If considered collectively, EU member states are the largest contributor of <a href="/wiki/List_of_development_aid_country_donors" title="List of development aid country donors">foreign aid</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GHA_report_2014_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-GHA_report_2014-212">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD_aid_report_2013_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECD_aid_report_2013-213">[185]</a></sup>
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ECHO_(European_Commission)" title="ECHO (European Commission)">European Commission's Humanitarian Aid and Civil Protection department</a>, or "ECHO", provides <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid" title="Humanitarian aid">humanitarian aid</a> from the EU to <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>. In 2012, its budget amounted to €874 million, 51% of the budget went to Africa and 20% to Asia, Latin America, the Caribbean and Pacific, and 20% to the Middle East and Mediterranean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>Humanitarian aid is financed directly by the budget (70%) as part of the financial instruments for external action and also by the <a href="/wiki/European_Development_Fund" title="European Development Fund">European Development Fund</a> (30%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-215">[187]</a></sup> The EU's external action financing is divided into 'geographic' instruments and 'thematic' instruments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_215-1"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-215">[187]</a></sup> The 'geographic' instruments provide aid through the <a href="/wiki/Development_Cooperation_Instrument" title="Development Cooperation Instrument">Development Cooperation Instrument</a> (DCI, €16.9 billion, 2007–2013), which must spend 95% of its budget on <a href="/wiki/Official_development_assistance" title="Official development assistance">official development assistance</a> (ODA), and from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_and_Partnership_Instrument" title="European Neighbourhood and Partnership Instrument">European Neighbourhood and Partnership Instrument</a> (ENPI), which contains some relevant programmes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_215-2"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-215">[187]</a></sup> The European Development Fund (EDF, €22.7 bn, 2008–2013) is made up of voluntary contributions by member states, but there is pressure to merge the EDF into the budget-financed instruments to encourage increased contributions to match the 0.7% target and allow the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> greater oversight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_215-3"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-215">[187]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, the average among EU countries was 0.4% and five had met or exceeded the 0.7% target: Denmark, Germany, Luxembourg, Sweden and the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[188]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_and_global_influence">Regional and global influence</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Eurosphere" title="Eurosphere">Eurosphere</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Union_as_an_emerging_superpower" title="European Union as an emerging superpower">European Union as an emerging superpower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europeanisation" title="Europeanisation">Europeanisation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="1880" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg/170px-Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg/255px-Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg/340px-Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eiffel_Tower" title="Eiffel Tower">Eiffel Tower</a>, Paris</div></div></div>
<p>Because of its ability to shape rules and norms on a global level as well as its attempts to influence neighbouring countries, the EU has been called an emerging or potential superpower by scholars and academics like T. R. Reid,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[189]</a></sup> Andrew Reding,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A._R._218-0"><a href="#cite_note-A._R.-218">[190]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Moravcsik" title="Andrew Moravcsik">Andrew Moravcsik</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[191]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Leonard_(director)" title="Mark Leonard (director)">Mark Leonard</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[192]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Rifkin" title="Jeremy Rifkin">Jeremy Rifkin</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[193]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_McCormick_(political_scientist)" title="John McCormick (political scientist)">John McCormick</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[194]</a></sup> and some politicians like <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[195]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[196]</a></sup> They believe that the EU is a superpower, or will become one, in the 21st century –  while noting that, for them, the concept of "superpower" has changed to one of <a href="/wiki/Soft_power" title="Soft power">soft power</a> rather than the hard (military) superpowers of the 20th century.
</p><p>The EU uses foreign relations instruments like the <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a> which seeks to tie those countries to the east and south of the European territory of the EU to the Union. These countries, primarily developing countries, include some who seek to one day become either a <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member state of the European Union</a>, or more closely integrated with the European Union. The EU offers financial assistance to countries within the European Neighbourhood, so long as they meet the strict conditions of government reform, economic reform and other issues surrounding positive transformation. This process is normally underpinned by an Action Plan, as agreed by both Brussels and the target country.
</p><p>Critics of the concept of the EU as an emerging superpower point to the lack of either a strong European military or of unified EU foreign policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[197]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_European_Union" title="Economy of the European Union">Economy of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regional_policy_of_the_European_Union" title="Regional policy of the European Union">Regional policy of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gross_domestic_product_(GDP)_per_inhabitant_in_purchasing_power_standards_(PPS)_in_relation_to_the_EU-28_average,_by_NUTS_2_regions,_2015.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1410" data-file-width="995" height="425" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Gross_domestic_product_%28GDP%29_per_inhabitant_in_purchasing_power_standards_%28PPS%29_in_relation_to_the_EU-28_average%2C_by_NUTS_2_regions%2C_2015.png/300px-Gross_domestic_product_%28GDP%29_per_inhabitant_in_purchasing_power_standards_%28PPS%29_in_relation_to_the_EU-28_average%2C_by_NUTS_2_regions%2C_2015.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Gross_domestic_product_%28GDP%29_per_inhabitant_in_purchasing_power_standards_%28PPS%29_in_relation_to_the_EU-28_average%2C_by_NUTS_2_regions%2C_2015.png/450px-Gross_domestic_product_%28GDP%29_per_inhabitant_in_purchasing_power_standards_%28PPS%29_in_relation_to_the_EU-28_average%2C_by_NUTS_2_regions%2C_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Gross_domestic_product_%28GDP%29_per_inhabitant_in_purchasing_power_standards_%28PPS%29_in_relation_to_the_EU-28_average%2C_by_NUTS_2_regions%2C_2015.png/600px-Gross_domestic_product_%28GDP%29_per_inhabitant_in_purchasing_power_standards_%28PPS%29_in_relation_to_the_EU-28_average%2C_by_NUTS_2_regions%2C_2015.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gross_domestic_product_(GDP)_per_inhabitant_in_purchasing_power_standards_(PPS)_in_relation_to_the_EU-28_average,_by_NUTS_2_regions,_2015.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gross domestic product (GDP) per inhabitant in purchasing power standards (PPS) in relation to the EU-28 average, by NUTS 2 regions, 2016</div></div></div>
<div class="thumbinner tright" style="width:300px; margin-left: 10px; margin-bottom: 10px;"><span style="display:inline-block; border:1px solid #ddd;"><div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_b1606c858a6684c69534f1afbe7f784a"></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/b1606c858a6684c69534f1afbe7f784a.png" usemap="#timeline_b1606c858a6684c69534f1afbe7f784a"/></div></span><div class="thumbcaption">The five largest economies in the world according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMF" title="IMF">IMF</a> by <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">Nominal GDP</a> in 2018<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[198]</a></sup></div></div>
<p>The European Union has established a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_market" title="Internal market">single market</a> across the territory of all its members representing 512 million citizens. In 2017, the EU had a combined GDP of $21 trillion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_dollar" title="International dollar">international dollars</a>, a 17% share of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP" title="List of countries by GDP">global gross domestic product by purchasing power parity (PPP)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011-IMG-GDP_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011-IMG-GDP-227">[199]</a></sup> As a political entity the European Union is represented in the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO). EU member states own the estimated second largest after the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a>93.6 trillion) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Net_wealth" title="Net wealth">net wealth</a> in the world, equal to 25% (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a>70.8 trillion) of the $280 trillion global wealth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[200]</a></sup>
</p><p>19 member states have joined a monetary union known as the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a>, which uses the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a> as a single currency. The currency union represents 342 million EU citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market-229">[201]</a></sup> The euro is the second largest <a href="/wiki/Reserve_currency" title="Reserve currency">reserve currency</a> as well as the second most traded currency in the world after the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[204]</a></sup>
</p><p>Of the top <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">500 largest corporations in the world measured by revenue</a> in 2010, 161 have their headquarters in the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[205]</a></sup> In 2016, unemployment in the EU stood at 8.9%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNEMP_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNEMP-234">[206]</a></sup> while inflation was at 2.2%, and the current account balance at −0.9% of GDP. The average annual net earnings in the European Union was around €24,000(US$30,000)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[207]</a></sup> in 2015, which was about 70% of that in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[208]</a></sup>
</p><p>
There is a significant variance for Nominal GDP per capita within individual EU states. The difference between the richest and poorest regions (276 NUTS-2 regions of the <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics</a>) ranged, in 2016, from 14%(Severozapaden, Bulgaria) of the EU28 average(€29,200) to 935%(Inner London - West, UK), or from €4,100 to €207,300.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[209]</a></sup></p><div style="clear:both;"></div>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px"><div style="width: 182px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Air_France_A380-800(F-HPJD)_(5233706017).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Air_France_A380-800%28F-HPJD%29_%285233706017%29.jpg/270px-Air_France_A380-800%28F-HPJD%29_%285233706017%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Air_France_A380-800%28F-HPJD%29_%285233706017%29.jpg/405px-Air_France_A380-800%28F-HPJD%29_%285233706017%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Air_France_A380-800%28F-HPJD%29_%285233706017%29.jpg/540px-Air_France_A380-800%28F-HPJD%29_%285233706017%29.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>World's largest passenger airplane <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> built by European corporation <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus SE</a>. Airbus is one of the world's leading aircraft manufacturers
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182.66666666667px"><div style="width: 182.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 180.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014-03-04_Geneva_Motor_Show_1377.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/2014-03-04_Geneva_Motor_Show_1377.JPG/271px-2014-03-04_Geneva_Motor_Show_1377.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/2014-03-04_Geneva_Motor_Show_1377.JPG/407px-2014-03-04_Geneva_Motor_Show_1377.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/2014-03-04_Geneva_Motor_Show_1377.JPG/542px-2014-03-04_Geneva_Motor_Show_1377.JPG 2x" width="181"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Automotive manufacturing is one of most enduring industrial activities in the EU, and it accounts for millions of jobs, billions of euros in investment, and represents a large portion of the continent's exports
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 195.33333333333px"><div style="width: 195.33333333333px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 193.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Bridge_(Karl%C5%AFv_most),_Vltava_River,_Prague,_2015.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2238" data-file-width="3600" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg/290px-Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg/435px-Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg/579px-Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg 2x" width="194"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Tourism is a major economic activity in the European Union with wide-ranging impact on economic growth and employment
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 177.33333333333px"><div style="width: 177.33333333333px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 175.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zicht_op_het_Delwaidedok.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="809" data-file-width="1181" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Zicht_op_het_Delwaidedok.jpg/263px-Zicht_op_het_Delwaidedok.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Zicht_op_het_Delwaidedok.jpg/394px-Zicht_op_het_Delwaidedok.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Zicht_op_het_Delwaidedok.jpg/526px-Zicht_op_het_Delwaidedok.jpg 2x" width="176"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Antwerp" title="Port of Antwerp">Port of Antwerp</a> container terminal, second-largest seaport in the European Union
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 219.33333333333px"><div style="width: 219.33333333333px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 217.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="4668" data-file-width="8442" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg/326px-City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg/489px-City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg/651px-City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg 2x" width="218"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a> is ranked as the world's second largest International Financial Centre behind New York
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Structural_Funds_and_Cohesion_Funds" title="Structural Funds and Cohesion Funds">Structural Funds and Cohesion Funds</a> are supporting the development of underdeveloped regions of the EU. Such regions are primarily located in the states of <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">central</a> and southern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Business2000_Funds_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-Business2000_Funds-239">[211]</a></sup> Several funds provide emergency aid, support for candidate members to transform their country to conform to the EU's standard (<a href="/wiki/Phare" title="Phare">Phare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Instrument_for_Structural_Policies_for_Pre-Accession" title="Instrument for Structural Policies for Pre-Accession">ISPA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Special_Accession_Programme_for_Agriculture_and_Rural_Development" title="Special Accession Programme for Agriculture and Rural Development">SAPARD</a>), and support to the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (<a href="/wiki/Technical_Aid_to_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Technical Aid to the Commonwealth of Independent States">TACIS</a>). TACIS has now become part of the worldwide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EuropeAid_Co-operation_Office" title="EuropeAid Co-operation Office">EuropeAid</a> programme. EU <a href="/wiki/Framework_Programmes_for_Research_and_Technological_Development" title="Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development">research and technological framework programmes</a> sponsor research conducted by consortia from all EU members to work towards a single <a href="/wiki/European_Research_Area" title="European Research Area">European Research Area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euractiv_FP7_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-Euractiv_FP7-240">[212]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_market">Internal market</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">European Single Market</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eirepas.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="842" data-file-width="600" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Eirepas.JPG/170px-Eirepas.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Eirepas.JPG/255px-Eirepas.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Eirepas.JPG/340px-Eirepas.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eirepas.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Passports_of_the_European_Union" title="Passports of the European Union">standardised passport</a> design, displaying the name of the member state, the national <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">arms</a> and the words "European Union" given in their official language(s). (Irish model)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DE_Licence_2013_Front.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2082" data-file-width="3210" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/DE_Licence_2013_Front.jpg/220px-DE_Licence_2013_Front.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/DE_Licence_2013_Front.jpg/330px-DE_Licence_2013_Front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/DE_Licence_2013_Front.jpg/440px-DE_Licence_2013_Front.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DE_Licence_2013_Front.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>German version of an <a href="/wiki/European_driving_licence" title="European driving licence">EU driving licence card</a> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_flag" title="EU flag">EU flag</a> on it</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Romanian_license_plate.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="79" data-file-width="347" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Romanian_license_plate.svg/220px-Romanian_license_plate.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Romanian_license_plate.svg/330px-Romanian_license_plate.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Romanian_license_plate.svg/440px-Romanian_license_plate.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Romanian_license_plate.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The common EU format of <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plates_of_Europe" title="Vehicle registration plates of Europe">vehicle registration plate</a><br/>(Romanian version pictured)</div></div></div>
<p>Two of the original core objectives of the European Economic Community were the development of a common market, subsequently becoming a <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">single market</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">customs union</a> between its member states. The single market involves <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_market" title="Internal market">the free circulation of goods, capital, people, and services within the EU</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_229-1"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market-229">[201]</a></sup> and the customs union involves the application of a <a href="/wiki/Common_external_tariff" title="Common external tariff">common external tariff</a> on all goods entering the market. Once goods have been admitted into the market they cannot be subjected to customs duties, discriminatory taxes or <a href="/wiki/Import_quota" title="Import quota">import quotas</a>, as they travel internally. The non-EU member states of <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> participate in the single market but not in the customs union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EEA_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-EEA-125">[110]</a></sup> Half the trade in the EU is covered by legislation harmonised by the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_G_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market_G-241">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>Free movement of capital is intended to permit movement of investments such as property purchases and buying of shares between countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_C_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market_C-242">[214]</a></sup> Until the drive towards <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_monetary_union" title="Economic and monetary union">economic and monetary union</a> the development of the capital provisions had been slow. Post-Maastricht there has been a rapidly developing corpus of ECJ judgements regarding this initially neglected freedom. The free movement of capital is unique insofar as it is granted equally to non-member states.
</p><p>The free movement of persons means that <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">EU citizens</a> can move freely between member states to live, work, study or retire in another country. This required the lowering of administrative formalities and recognition of professional qualifications of other states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_P_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market_P-243">[215]</a></sup>
</p><p>The free movement of services and of establishment allows self-employed persons to move between member states to provide services on a temporary or permanent basis. While services account for 60–70% of GDP, legislation in the area is not as developed as in other areas. This lacuna has been addressed by the recently passed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Directive_on_services_in_the_internal_market" title="Directive on services in the internal market">Directive on services in the internal market</a> which aims to liberalise the cross border provision of services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_S_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market_S-244">[216]</a></sup> According to the Treaty the provision of services is a residual freedom that only applies if no other freedom is being exercised.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monetary_union">Monetary union</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Monetary_Union_of_the_European_Union" title="Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union">Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_13.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="3622" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_13.jpg/170px-European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_13.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_13.jpg/255px-European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_13.jpg/340px-European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_13.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_Central_Bank_-_building_under_construction_-_Frankfurt_-_Germany_-_13.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_the_European_Central_Bank" title="Seat of the European Central Bank">seat of the European Central Bank</a> in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>. 19 of the 28 EU member states have adopted the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> as their <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">legal tender</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="645" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/220px-BlueEurozone.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/330px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/440px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> (dark blue) represents 340 million people. The euro is the second-largest reserve currency in the world.</div></div></div>
<p>The creation of a <a href="/wiki/European_Currency_Unit" title="European Currency Unit">European single currency</a> became an official objective of the European Economic Community in 1969. In 1992, having negotiated the structure and procedures of a currency union, the member states signed the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> and were legally bound to fulfil the agreed-on rules including the <a href="/wiki/Euro_convergence_criteria" title="Euro convergence criteria">convergence criteria</a> if they wanted to join the <a href="/wiki/Currency_union" title="Currency union">monetary union</a>. The states wanting to participate had first to join the <a href="/wiki/European_Exchange_Rate_Mechanism" title="European Exchange Rate Mechanism">European Exchange Rate Mechanism</a>.
</p><p>In 1999 the currency union started, first as an accounting currency with <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_euro" title="History of the euro">eleven member states</a> joining. In 2002, the currency was fully put into place, when <a href="/wiki/Euro_banknotes" title="Euro banknotes">euro notes</a> and coins were issued and national currencies began to phase out in the eurozone, which by then consisted of 12 member states. The eurozone (constituted by the EU member states which have adopted the euro) has since grown to 19 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[ac]</a></sup>
</p><p>The euro, and the monetary policies of those who have adopted it in agreement with the EU, are under the control of the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> (ECB).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[218]</a></sup> The ECB is the central bank for the eurozone, and thus controls <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary policy</a> in that area with an agenda to maintain <a href="/wiki/Price_stability" title="Price stability">price stability</a>. It is at the centre of the <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Central_Banks" title="European System of Central Banks">European System of Central Banks</a>, which comprehends all EU national central banks and is controlled by its General Council, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Central_Bank" title="President of the European Central Bank">President of the ECB</a>, who is appointed by the European Council, the Vice-President of the ECB, and the governors of the national central banks of all 28 EU member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECB_org_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-ECB_org-248">[219]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Financial_Supervision" title="European System of Financial Supervision">European System of Financial Supervision</a> is an institutional architecture of the EU's framework of financial supervision composed by three authorities: the <a href="/wiki/European_Banking_Authority" title="European Banking Authority">European Banking Authority</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Insurance_and_Occupational_Pensions_Authority" title="European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority">European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Securities_and_Markets_Authority" title="European Securities and Markets Authority">European Securities and Markets Authority</a>. To complement this framework, there is also a <a href="/wiki/European_Systemic_Risk_Board" title="European Systemic Risk Board">European Systemic Risk Board</a> under the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">ECB</a>. The aim of this financial control system is to ensure the economic stability of the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[220]</a></sup>
</p><p>To prevent the joining states from getting into financial trouble or crisis after entering the monetary union, they were obliged in the Maastricht treaty to fulfil important financial obligations and procedures, especially to show budgetary discipline and a high degree of sustainable economic convergence, as well as to avoid excessive government deficits and limit the government debt to a sustainable level.
</p>

</div>
<p>In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_2005" title="Treaty of Accession 2005">EU-27</a> had a gross inland energy consumption of 1,825 million tonnes of oil equivalent (toe).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EurostatEnergy_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-EurostatEnergy-251">[221]</a></sup> Around 46% of the energy consumed was produced within the member states while 54% was imported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EurostatEnergy_251-1"><a href="#cite_note-EurostatEnergy-251">[221]</a></sup> In these statistics, nuclear energy is treated as <a href="/wiki/Primary_energy" title="Primary energy">primary energy</a> produced in the EU, regardless of the source of the uranium, of which less than 3% is produced in the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euratom2007_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-Euratom2007-252">[222]</a></sup>
</p><p>The EU has had legislative power in the area of energy policy for most of its existence; this has its roots in the original <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>. The introduction of a mandatory and comprehensive European energy policy was approved at the meeting of the European Council in October 2005, and the first draft policy was published in January 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Energy_Q&amp;A_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_Q&amp;A-253">[223]</a></sup>
</p><p>The EU has five key points in its energy policy: increase competition in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_market" title="Internal market">internal market</a>, encourage investment and boost interconnections between electricity grids; diversify energy resources with better systems to respond to a crisis; establish a new treaty framework for energy co-operation with Russia while improving relations with energy-rich states in Central Asia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oies_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-oies-254">[224]</a></sup> and North Africa; use existing energy supplies more efficiently while increasing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialisation" title="Renewable energy commercialisation">renewable energy commercialisation</a>; and finally increase funding for new energy technologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Energy_Q&amp;A_253-1"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_Q&amp;A-253">[223]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, EU countries as a whole imported 82% of their oil, 57% of their natural gas<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-low_carb_prop_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-low_carb_prop-255">[225]</a></sup> and 97.48% of their uranium<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euratom2007_252-1"><a href="#cite_note-Euratom2007-252">[222]</a></sup> demands. There is a strong <a href="/wiki/Russia_in_the_European_energy_sector" title="Russia in the European energy sector">dependence on Russian energy</a> that the EU has been attempting to reduce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Energy_Russia_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_Russia-256">[226]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Transport" title="European Commissioner for Transport">European Commissioner for Transport</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Industry_and_Entrepreneurship" title="European Commissioner for Industry and Entrepreneurship">European Commissioner for Industry and Entrepreneurship</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a></div><p>The EU is working to improve cross-border infrastructure within the EU, for example through the <a href="/wiki/Trans-European_Networks" title="Trans-European Networks">Trans-European Networks</a> (TEN). Projects under TEN include the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGV_Est" title="LGV Est">LGV Est</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9jus_Rail_Tunnel" title="Fréjus Rail Tunnel">Fréjus Rail Tunnel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund_Bridge" title="Øresund Bridge">Öresund Bridge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brenner_Base_Tunnel" title="Brenner Base Tunnel">Brenner Base Tunnel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Messina_Bridge" title="Strait of Messina Bridge">Strait of Messina Bridge</a>. In 2010 the estimated network covers: 75,200 kilometres (46,700 mi) of roads; 78,000 kilometres (48,000 mi) of railways; 330 airports; 270 maritime harbours; and 210 internal harbours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[227]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[228]</a></sup>
</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europe_Completed_Motorways_Dec_2012.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1604" data-file-width="2000" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Europe_Completed_Motorways_Dec_2012.png/220px-Europe_Completed_Motorways_Dec_2012.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Europe_Completed_Motorways_Dec_2012.png/330px-Europe_Completed_Motorways_Dec_2012.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Europe_Completed_Motorways_Dec_2012.png/440px-Europe_Completed_Motorways_Dec_2012.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europe_Completed_Motorways_Dec_2012.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Approximate extent of completed motorway network in Europe as of March 2016</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Europe" title="Rail transport in Europe">Rail transport in Europe</a> is being synchronised with the <a href="/wiki/European_Rail_Traffic_Management_System" title="European Rail Traffic Management System">European Rail Traffic Management System</a> (ERTMS), an initiative to greatly enhance safety, increase efficiency of trains and enhance cross-border interoperability of rail transport in Europe by replacing signalling equipment with digitised mostly wireless versions and by creating a single Europe-wide standard for train control and command systems.
</p><p>The developing European transport policies will increase the pressure on the environment in many regions by the increased transport network. In the pre-2004 EU members, the major problem in transport deals with congestion and pollution. After the recent enlargement, the new states that joined since 2004 added the problem of solving accessibility to the transport agenda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[229]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Highways_in_Poland" title="Highways in Poland">Polish road network</a> was upgraded such as the <a href="/wiki/A4_autostrada_(Poland)" title="A4 autostrada (Poland)">A4 autostrada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[230]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(satellite_navigation)" title="Galileo (satellite navigation)">Galileo positioning system</a> is another EU infrastructure project. Galileo is a proposed <a href="/wiki/Satellite_navigation" title="Satellite navigation">Satellite navigation</a> system, to be built by the EU and launched by the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> (ESA). The Galileo project was launched partly to reduce the EU's dependency on the US-operated <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">Global Positioning System</a>, but also to give more complete global coverage and allow for greater accuracy, given the aged nature of the GPS system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barrot_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barrot-261">[231]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">

</p>
</div>
