<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg/220px-RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg/330px-RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg/440px-RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vineyards in <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>; EU farms are supported by the <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">budgetary</a> expenditure.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a> (CAP) is one of the long lasting policies of the European Community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stead_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-stead-262">[232]</a></sup> The policy has the objectives of increasing agricultural production, providing certainty in food supplies, ensuring a high quality of life for farmers, stabilising markets, and ensuring reasonable prices for consumers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[ae]</a></sup> It was, until recently, operated by a system of subsidies and market intervention. Until the 1990s, the policy accounted for over 60% of the then <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Community</a>'s annual budget, and as of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=European_Union&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> accounts for around 34%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU_CAP_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-EU_CAP-264">[233]</a></sup>
</p><p>The policy's <a href="/wiki/Incomes_policy" title="Incomes policy">price controls</a> and market interventions led to considerable <a href="/wiki/Overproduction" title="Overproduction">overproduction</a>. These were <a href="/wiki/Buffer_stock_scheme" title="Buffer stock scheme">intervention stores</a> of products bought up by the Community to maintain minimum price levels. To dispose of surplus stores, they were often sold on the world market at prices considerably below Community guaranteed prices, or farmers were offered subsidies (amounting to the difference between the Community and world prices) to export their products outside the Community. This system has been criticised for under-cutting farmers outside Europe, especially those in the <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">developing world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_CAP_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_CAP-265">[234]</a></sup> Supporters of CAP argue that the economic support which it gives to farmers provides them with a reasonable standard of living.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_CAP_265-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_CAP-265">[234]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the beginning of the 1990s, the CAP has been subject to a series of reforms. Initially, these reforms included the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Set-aside" title="Set-aside">set-aside</a> in 1988, where a proportion of farm land was deliberately withdrawn from production, milk quotas and, more recently, the 'de-coupling' (or disassociation) of the money farmers receive from the EU and the amount they produce (by the Fischler reforms in 2004). Agriculture expenditure will move away from subsidy payments linked to specific produce, toward direct payments based on farm size. This is intended to allow the market to dictate production levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stead_262-1"><a href="#cite_note-stead-262">[232]</a></sup> One of these reforms entailed the modification of the EU's sugar regime, which previously divided the sugar market between member states and certain African-Caribbean nations with a privileged relationship with the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_CAP_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-EC_CAP-266">[235]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/European_Union_competition_law" title="European Union competition law">European Union competition law</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Competition" title="European Commissioner for Competition">European Commissioner for Competition</a></div>
<p>The EU operates a <a href="/wiki/European_Union_competition_law" title="European Union competition law">competition policy</a> intended to ensure undistorted competition within the single market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[af]</a></sup> The Commission as the competition regulator for the single market is responsible for antitrust issues, approving <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">mergers</a>, breaking up cartels, working for <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">economic liberalisation</a> and preventing <a href="/wiki/Subsidy" title="Subsidy">state aid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[236]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2017)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Competition" title="European Commissioner for Competition">Competition Commissioner</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_Vestager" title="Margrethe Vestager">Margrethe Vestager</a>, is one of the most powerful positions in the Commission, notable for the ability to affect the commercial interests of trans-national corporations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[237]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2017)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> For example, in 2001 the Commission for the first time prevented a merger between two companies based in the United States (<a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">GE</a> and <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a>) which had already been approved by their national authority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[238]</a></sup> Another high-profile case <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Union_Microsoft_competition_case" title="European Union Microsoft competition case">against Microsoft</a>, resulted in the Commission fining <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> over €777 million following nine years of legal action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[239]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_policy">Social policy</span></h2>
<p>The EU has long sought to mitigate the effects of free markets by protecting workers rights and preventing social and environmental dumping. To this end it has adopted laws establishing minimun employment and environmental standards. These included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Working_Time_Directive" title="Working Time Directive">Working Time Directive</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Impact_Assessment_Directive_2011" title="Environmental Impact Assessment Directive 2011">Environmental Impact Assessment Directive</a>. The EU has also sought to coordinate the social security and health systems of member states to facilitate individuals exercising free movement rights and to ensure they maintain their ability to access social security and health services in other member states.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_the_Environment" title="European Commissioner for the Environment">European Commissioner for the Environment</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Climate_Change_Programme" title="European Climate Change Programme">European Climate Change Programme</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hajn%C3%B3wka,_Poland_-_panoramio_(73).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Hajn%C3%B3wka%2C_Poland_-_panoramio_%2873%29.jpg/220px-Hajn%C3%B3wka%2C_Poland_-_panoramio_%2873%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Hajn%C3%B3wka%2C_Poland_-_panoramio_%2873%29.jpg/330px-Hajn%C3%B3wka%2C_Poland_-_panoramio_%2873%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Hajn%C3%B3wka%2C_Poland_-_panoramio_%2873%29.jpg/440px-Hajn%C3%B3wka%2C_Poland_-_panoramio_%2873%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hajn%C3%B3wka,_Poland_-_panoramio_(73).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/European_bison" title="European bison">Bison</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Białowieża Forest">Białowieża Forest</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_land_area_of_different_European_countries_covered_by_Forest.pdf"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3582" data-file-width="4261" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Percentage_of_land_area_of_different_European_countries_covered_by_Forest.pdf/page1-200px-Percentage_of_land_area_of_different_European_countries_covered_by_Forest.pdf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Percentage_of_land_area_of_different_European_countries_covered_by_Forest.pdf/page1-300px-Percentage_of_land_area_of_different_European_countries_covered_by_Forest.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Percentage_of_land_area_of_different_European_countries_covered_by_Forest.pdf/page1-400px-Percentage_of_land_area_of_different_European_countries_covered_by_Forest.pdf.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_land_area_of_different_European_countries_covered_by_Forest.pdf" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Percentage of land area of different European countries covered by forest</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="361" data-file-width="512" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg/200px-European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg/300px-European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg/400px-European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Biogeography" title="Biogeography">Biogeographic regions</a> of the continental European Union, according to the <a href="/wiki/European_Environment_Agency" title="European Environment Agency">European Environmental Agency</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1957, when the EEC was founded, it had no environmental policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[240]</a></sup> Over the past 50 years, an increasingly dense network of legislation has been created, extending to all areas of environmental protection, including air pollution, water quality, waste management, nature conservation, and the control of chemicals, industrial hazards, and biotechnology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[241]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_European_Environmental_Policy" title="Institute for European Environmental Policy">Institute for European Environmental Policy</a>, environmental law comprises over 500 Directives, Regulations and Decisions, making environmental policy a core area of European politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Environmental_Policy_2012_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-European_Environmental_Policy_2012-274">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p>European policy-makers originally increased the EU's capacity to act on environmental issues by defining it as a trade problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[243]</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Trade_barrier" title="Trade barrier">Trade barriers</a> and competitive distortions in the Common Market could emerge due to the different environmental standards in each member state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[244]</a></sup> In subsequent years, the environment became a formal policy area, with its own policy actors, principles and procedures. The legal basis for EU environmental policy was established with the introduction of the Single European Act in 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Environmental_Policy_2012_274-1"><a href="#cite_note-European_Environmental_Policy_2012-274">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p>Initially, EU environmental policy focused on Europe. More recently, the EU has demonstrated leadership in global environmental governance, e.g. the role of the EU in securing the ratification and coming into force of the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> despite opposition from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. This international dimension is reflected in the EU's Sixth Environmental Action Programme,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[245]</a></sup> which recognises that its objectives can only be achieved if key international agreements are actively supported and properly implemented both at EU level and worldwide. The Lisbon Treaty further strengthened the leadership ambitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[246]</a></sup> EU law has played a significant role in improving habitat and species protection in Europe, as well as contributing to improvements in air and water quality and waste management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Environmental_Policy_2012_274-2"><a href="#cite_note-European_Environmental_Policy_2012-274">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mitigating <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> is one of the top priorities of EU environmental policy. In 2007, member states agreed that, in the future, 20% of the energy used across the EU must be <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable</a>, and carbon dioxide emissions have to be lower in 2020 by at least 20% compared to 1990 levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUO_energy_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUO_energy-279">[247]</a></sup>  The EU has adopted an <a href="/wiki/Emissions_trading" title="Emissions trading">emissions trading system</a> to incorporate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_emissions" title="Carbon emissions">carbon emissions</a> into the economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[248]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Green_Capital" title="European Green Capital">European Green Capital</a> is an annual award given to cities that focuses on the environment, energy efficiency, and quality of life in urban areas to create <a href="/wiki/Smart_city" title="Smart city">smart city</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_science">Education and science</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Educational_policies_and_initiatives_of_the_European_Union" title="Educational policies and initiatives of the European Union">Educational policies and initiatives of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Framework_Programmes_for_Research_and_Technological_Development" title="Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development">Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Holbein-erasmus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1145" data-file-width="809" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Holbein-erasmus.jpg/150px-Holbein-erasmus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Holbein-erasmus.jpg/225px-Holbein-erasmus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Holbein-erasmus.jpg/300px-Holbein-erasmus.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Holbein-erasmus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Desiderius_Erasmus_of_Rotterdam" title="Desiderius Erasmus of Rotterdam">Desiderius Erasmus of Rotterdam</a>, renacentist humanist that gave name to <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Programme" title="Erasmus Programme">Erasmus Programme</a></div></div></div>
<p>Basic education is an area where the EU's role is limited to supporting national governments. In higher education, the policy was developed in the 1980s in programmes supporting exchanges and mobility. The most visible of these has been the <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Programme" title="Erasmus Programme">Erasmus Programme</a>, a university exchange programme which began in 1987. In its first 20 years, it supported international exchange opportunities for well over 1.5 million university and college students and became a symbol of European student life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[249]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are similar programmes for school pupils and teachers, for trainees in <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational education and training</a>, and for adult learners in the <a href="/wiki/Lifelong_Learning_Programme_2007%E2%80%932013" title="Lifelong Learning Programme 2007–2013">Lifelong Learning Programme 2007–2013</a>. These programmes are designed to encourage a wider knowledge of other countries and to spread good practices in the education and training fields across the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[251]</a></sup> Through its support of the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Process" title="Bologna Process">Bologna Process</a>, the EU is supporting comparable standards and compatible degrees across Europe.
</p><p>Scientific development is facilitated through the EU's <a href="/wiki/Framework_Programmes_for_Research_and_Technological_Development" title="Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development">Framework Programmes</a>, the first of which started in 1984. The aims of EU policy in this area are to co-ordinate and stimulate research. The independent <a href="/wiki/European_Research_Council" title="European Research Council">European Research Council</a> allocates EU funds to European or national research projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[252]</a></sup> EU <a href="/wiki/Framework_Programmes_for_Research_and_Technological_Development" title="Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development">research and technological framework programmes</a> deal in a number of areas, for example energy where the aim is to develop a diverse mix of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> to help the environment and to reduce dependence on imported fuels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[253]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Europe" title="Healthcare in Europe">Healthcare in Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="626" data-file-width="1000" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg/220px-Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg/330px-Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg/440px-Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carte_Europ%C3%A9enne_d%27Assurance_Maladie_France.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/European_Health_Insurance_Card" title="European Health Insurance Card">European Health Insurance Card</a><br/>(French version pictured)</div></div></div>
<p>Although the EU has no major competences in the field of health care, Article 35 of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union</a> affirms that "A high level of human health protection shall be ensured in the definition and implementation of all Union policies and activities". The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_Health_and_Consumers_(European_Commission)" title="Directorate-General for Health and Consumers (European Commission)">Directorate-General for Health and Consumers</a> seeks to align national laws on the protection of people's health, on the consumers' rights, on the safety of food and other products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[254]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[255]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[256]</a></sup>
</p><p>All EU and many other European countries offer their citizens a free <a href="/wiki/European_Health_Insurance_Card" title="European Health Insurance Card">European Health Insurance Card</a> which, on a reciprocal basis, provides insurance for emergency medical treatment insurance when visiting other participating European countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[257]</a></sup> A directive on cross-border healthcare aims at promoting co-operation on health care between member states and facilitating access to safe and high-quality cross-border healthcare for European patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[259]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[260]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Europe" title="Culture of Europe">Culture of Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western culture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_policies_of_the_European_Union" title="Cultural policies of the European Union">Cultural policies of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_of_the_Acropolis_Athens_2_(pixinn.net).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1156" data-file-width="1920" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/View_of_the_Acropolis_Athens_2_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/220px-View_of_the_Acropolis_Athens_2_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/View_of_the_Acropolis_Athens_2_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/330px-View_of_the_Acropolis_Athens_2_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/View_of_the_Acropolis_Athens_2_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/440px-View_of_the_Acropolis_Athens_2_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:View_of_the_Acropolis_Athens_2_(pixinn.net).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> programme was launched in the summer of 1985 with <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> being the first title-holder</div></div></div>
<p>Cultural co-operation between member states has been a concern of the EU since its inclusion as a community competency in the Maastricht Treaty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bozoki_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bozoki-293">[261]</a></sup> Actions taken in the cultural area by the EU include the <a href="/wiki/Culture_2000" title="Culture 2000">Culture 2000</a> seven-year programme,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bozoki_293-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bozoki-293">[261]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/European_Cultural_Month" title="European Cultural Month">European Cultural Month</a> event,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Culture_Month_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-Culture_Month-294">[262]</a></sup> and orchestras such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Youth_Orchestra" title="European Union Youth Orchestra">European Union Youth Orchestra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[263]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> programme selects one or more cities in every year to assist the <a href="/wiki/Sociocultural_evolution" title="Sociocultural evolution">cultural development</a> of that city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Capital_Culture_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-Capital_Culture-296">[264]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_policies_of_the_European_Union" title="Sport policies of the European Union">Sport policies of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Giro_d%27Italia_2012,_072_pampeago_rodriguez_met_puffertje_(17786750665).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1241" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Giro_d%27Italia_2012%2C_072_pampeago_rodriguez_met_puffertje_%2817786750665%29.jpg/220px-Giro_d%27Italia_2012%2C_072_pampeago_rodriguez_met_puffertje_%2817786750665%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Giro_d%27Italia_2012%2C_072_pampeago_rodriguez_met_puffertje_%2817786750665%29.jpg/330px-Giro_d%27Italia_2012%2C_072_pampeago_rodriguez_met_puffertje_%2817786750665%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Giro_d%27Italia_2012%2C_072_pampeago_rodriguez_met_puffertje_%2817786750665%29.jpg/440px-Giro_d%27Italia_2012%2C_072_pampeago_rodriguez_met_puffertje_%2817786750665%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Giro_d%27Italia_2012,_072_pampeago_rodriguez_met_puffertje_(17786750665).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Starting in 1909, the <a href="/wiki/Giro_d%27Italia" title="Giro d'Italia">Giro d'Italia</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tour_(cycling)" title="Grand Tour (cycling)">Grands Tours</a>' second oldest<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[265]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is by far the most popular sport in the European Union by the number of registered players. The other sports with the most participants in clubs are tennis, swimming, athletics, golf, gymnastics, equestrian sports, handball, volleyball and sailing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[266]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sport is mainly the responsibility of the member states or other international organisations, rather than of the EU. However, there are some EU policies that have affected sport, such as the free movement of workers, which was at the core of the <a href="/wiki/Bosman_ruling" title="Bosman ruling">Bosman ruling</a> that prohibited national football leagues from imposing quotas on foreign players with European citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Boseman_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Boseman-299">[267]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> requires any application of economic rules to take into account the specific nature of sport and its structures based on voluntary activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[268]</a></sup> This followed lobbying by governing organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> and <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, due to objections over the application of free market principles to sport, which led to an increasing gap between rich and poor clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHT_RT_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-IHT_RT-301">[269]</a></sup> The EU does fund a programme for Israeli, Jordanian, Irish, and British football coaches, as part of the Football 4 Peace project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[270]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3564" data-file-width="2443" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg/170px-Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg/255px-Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg/340px-Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bust_of_Charlemagne" title="Bust of Charlemagne">Bust of Charlemagne</a> with the German <i><a href="/wiki/Reichsadler" title="Reichsadler">Reichsadler</a></i> embossed on the metal and the French <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lis" title="Fleur-de-lis">fleur-de-lis</a> embroidered on the fabric. <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Cathedral_Treasury" title="Aachen Cathedral Treasury">Aachen Cathedral Treasury</a></div></div></div>
<p>The flag used is the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">Flag of Europe</a>, which consists of a <a href="/wiki/Circle_of_stars" title="Circle of stars">circle of</a> 12 golden stars on a blue background. The blue represents the West, while the number and position of the stars represent completeness and unity, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36th_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-36th-303">[271]</a></sup> Originally designed in 1955 for the Council of Europe, the flag was adopted by the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a>, the predecessors of the present Union, in 1986.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Motto_of_the_European_Union" title="Motto of the European Union">United in Diversity</a></i> was adopted as the motto of the Union in the year 2000, having been selected from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_motto_for_Europe" title="A motto for Europe">proposals</a> submitted by school pupils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimons2002110_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimons2002110-304">[272]</a></sup> Since 1985, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flag_day" title="Flag day">flag day</a> of the Union has been <a href="/wiki/Europe_Day" title="Europe Day">Europe Day</a>, on 9 May (the date of the 1950 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schuman_declaration" title="Schuman declaration">Schuman declaration</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Anthem_of_Europe" title="Anthem of Europe">anthem of the Union</a> is an instrumental version of the prelude to the <i><a href="/wiki/Ode_to_Joy" title="Ode to Joy">Ode to Joy</a></i>, the 4th movement of <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._9_(Beethoven)" title="Symphony No. 9 (Beethoven)">ninth symphony</a>. The anthem was adopted by European Community leaders in 1985 and has since been played on official occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[273]</a></sup>
</p><p>Besides naming the continent, the <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">Greek mythological</a> figure of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europa_(mythology)" title="Europa (mythology)">Europa</a> has frequently been employed as a <a href="/wiki/National_personification" title="National personification">personification</a> of Europe. Known from the myth in which <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">Zeus</a> seduces her in the guise of a white bull, Europa has also been referred to in relation to the present Union. Statues of Europa and the bull decorate several of the Union's institutions and a portrait of her is seen on the 2013 series of <a href="/wiki/Euro_banknotes" title="Euro banknotes">Euro banknotes</a>. The bull is, for its part, depicted on all residence permit cards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDemey2007387_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDemey2007387-306">[274]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Abduction_of_Europa,_Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Troy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3204" data-file-width="4000" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/The_Abduction_of_Europa%2C_Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Troy.jpg/220px-The_Abduction_of_Europa%2C_Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Troy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/The_Abduction_of_Europa%2C_Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Troy.jpg/330px-The_Abduction_of_Europa%2C_Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Troy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/The_Abduction_of_Europa%2C_Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Troy.jpg/440px-The_Abduction_of_Europa%2C_Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Troy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Abduction_of_Europa,_Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Troy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europa_(mythology)" title="Europa (mythology)">Europa</a> and the bull, depicted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Troy" title="Jean-François de Troy">Jean-François de Troy</a> (1716)</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charles the Great</a>, also known as Charlemagne (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">Carolus Magnus</i>) and later recognised as <i>Pater Europae</i> ("Father of Europe"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_307-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-307">[275]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[276]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[277]</a></sup> has a symbolic relevance to Europe. The Commission has named <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne_building" title="Charlemagne building">one of its central buildings</a> in Brussels after Charlemagne and the city of <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> has since 1949 awarded the <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne_Prize" title="Charlemagne Prize">Charlemagne Prize</a> to champions of European unification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[278]</a></sup> Since 2008, the organisers of this prize, in conjunction with the European Parliament, have awarded the <a href="/wiki/European_Charlemagne_Youth_Prize" title="European Charlemagne Youth Prize">Charlemagne Youth Prize</a> in recognition of similar efforts by young people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[279]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1997, Polish-born <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> canonised Poland's 14th-century monarch <a href="/wiki/Jadwiga_of_Poland" title="Jadwiga of Poland">Jadwiga</a> as Saint Hedwig, the <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> of queens and of European unification<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[280]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (July 2018)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_freedom_in_the_European_Union" title="Media freedom in the European Union">Media freedom in the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1366" data-file-width="2048" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg/220px-Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg/330px-Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg/440px-Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Euronews" title="Euronews">Euronews</a> headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a></div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_freedom" title="Media freedom">Media freedom</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_rights" title="Fundamental rights">fundamental right</a> that applies to all <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member states</a> of the European Union and its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_citizens" title="EU citizens">citizens</a>, as defined in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights" title="EU Charter of Fundamental Rights">EU Charter of Fundamental Rights</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eprs_313-0"><a href="#cite_note-eprs-313">[281]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>1</span></sup> Within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_enlargement" title="EU enlargement">EU enlargement</a> process, guaranteeing media freedom is named a "key indicator of a country's readiness to become part of the EU".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[282]</a></sup>
</p><p>The vast majority of media in the European Union are national-oriented. However, some EU-wide media focusing on European affairs have emerged since the early 1990s, such as <a href="/wiki/Euronews" title="Euronews">Euronews</a>, <a href="/wiki/EUobserver" title="EUobserver">EUobserver</a>, <a href="/wiki/EURACTIV" title="EURACTIV">EURACTIV</a> or <a href="/wiki/Politico_Europe" title="Politico Europe">Politico Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[283]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arte" title="Arte">ARTE</a> is a public Franco-German TV network that promotes programming in the areas of culture and the arts. 80% of its programming are provided in equal proportion by the two member companies, while the remainder is being provided by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Economic_Interest_Grouping" title="European Economic Interest Grouping">European Economic Interest Grouping</a> <i>ARTE GEIE</i> and the channel's European partners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[284]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/MEDIA_Programme" title="MEDIA Programme">MEDIA Programme</a> of the European Union intends to support the European popular film and audiovisual industries since 1991. It provides support for the development, promotion and distribution of European works within Europe and beyond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[285]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Current Article 1 of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Maastricht" title="Treaty of Maastricht">Treaty on European Union</a> reads: "The Union shall be founded on the present Treaty and on the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union</a>. Those <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_EU" title="Treaties of the EU">two Treaties</a> shall have the same legal value. The Union shall replace and succeed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Community" title="European Community">European Community</a>".</span>

<li id="cite_note-207"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-207">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/world/news/article.cfm?c_id=2&amp;objectid=10685127" rel="nofollow">"Britain and France to work together"</a> by Catherine Field. 4 November 2010. nzherald.co.nz. According to the Stockholm International Peace Research Institute (SIPRI), Britain spent more than US$69 billion on defence last year, placing it third in the world after the United States and China, while France spent US$67.31 billion, the fourth largest. Together, Britain and France account for 45 per cent of Europe's defence budget, 50 per cent of its military capacity and 70 per cent of all spending in military research and development. Copyright 2010, APN Holdings NZ Limited.</span>
</li>
